# Story so far

# Chapter 00 Neverwinter Expansionism and the North, Excerpt from the Great Sage Konstantinious the 12th

With the great sundering complete, the people of the Realms hoped that the era of mischief from the gods walking the world would end. 

The gods, however, read the rules, and the rules of Aos always have exceptions. And the existence of those exceptions convinced the gods to try. 

First, Tiamat, co-resident of Avernus, duped Severin and the Cult of the Dragon to attempt to bring her into the world. Tiamat thought the plan was hers, but it wasn’t. It was Zariel who found the loophole. It was Zariel who was tired of Tiamat’s presence in her kingdom. Zariel had other plans. 

Then it was the All-Father, god of the giants, who fantasized about a north that the Giants ruled. And in the chaos that his plans created, the Great Ancient Blue Dragon almost destroyed the kingdoms of the giants. And from Amn’s plans, other plans became possible and were thwarted. 

The sage KP found a piece of the artifact that he needed. The Kraken society was revealed and survived. The Lord’s Alliance grew in strength. The Storm Giant King Hekaton created an alliance between giants and the people of the realms. 

As for Ilymrith, she escaped. 

But twice, the plans of the gods had been thwarted[^1]. Twice, the gods had interfered. 

The people of the realms had hoped it would end here. And it did not. 

This time it was Lolth. Trapped in a demi-plane as part of an elaborate multi-century plan, she was thought finished. But Lolth was a schemer, and she always had contingency plans. Her plan required magic that could temporarily loosen the bonds holding the planes separate. Her pawn was Gromph Baenre of the First House of Menozberanzan. 

The spell twisted the magic of the Faerzess, an unknown magical substance that grows in the Underdark and acts as a naturally occurring forbiddance. Gromph Baenre thought it would give the Drow control of the Faerzess, allowing them to attack at will other powers. He was wrong. 

Instead, the bonds between the Abyss and Toril weakened for a moment. And the demon lords entered the Underdark.  

Both the world below and above were in turmoil. The demon Grazz’t instigated widespread insanity and madness, while the demoness Zugtomy disseminated perilous fungi. The demon Orcus marshaled armies of undead, and reports indicate that Demogorgon wreaked havoc on cities, including the notable city of Menozberranzan. 

The chaos in the Underdark may have provoked the Uthgartd Barbarians to launch a devastating assault on the North, destroying numerous smaller communities. Triboar was razed, Calling Horn was obliterated, and several villages on the outskirts of Silverymoon and Mirabar were pillaged.

Despite these dire circumstances, hope was not entirely lost. Following the War of the Dragons, the Northern Territories and the Lord’s Alliance forces were recovering from their conclusive battle against the Cult of the Dragon. Had the Ordning not been reinstated, and had the Giants initiated an assault on the cities, the outcome would have been catastrophic. However, with the re-establishment of the Ordning, the armies were intact. [^2]

Additionally, the alliance of the Silvery Marches was revived due to the efforts of several agents from Everlund. 

The combined strength of the Giants and major cities successfully ended the barbarian invasion. 

With the threat over and the elimination of the Barbarians from the hinterland, Lord Nevermember has turned his eye to the hinterland of his city-state. 

In particular, the town of Phandalin. He needed the area cleared of monsters, cults, and evildoers to encourage settlement and growth. 

Because of the costs of the wars, he decided to use adventurers, offering them tax-free no no-questions-asked plunder. One of those adventurers was an avant-garde[^3] musician whose music was underappreciated – Vukardin. 

# Chapter 01 Arrival in Phandalin 

## 

## 1/1 of Taraksh 1495

### Vukardin 

Vukradin’s music was once again not earning coin. An artist is never appreciated in his time, and yet an artist must eat. 

He stared at his audience in the First Flophouse in the Heapside. Other than the Brewbarry, the Uthgardian barbarian, no one was listening. 

“How did I end up here? The only people who show up here are those who want the cheapest night and drink they can find.”

He tries not to stare at the customers with a reputation for making darker deals than finding some company. 

#### *Flashback 8/3 of Ches1495*

“I need some money,” and he remembers his discussion with the Wintershield watchman. The meeting had left him unsettled. 

“I can make money by going to Phandelin?” 

“Yes,” had said the guard. “Clear the area of monsters and evildoers, and keep the treasure you find.”

“But doesn’t the treasure belong to someone else? Shouldn’t we return it to its original owners?” 

The guard had stared at him, exasperated \- “Look, I don’t make the rules, I just post them.” 

“But if these monsters or brigands stole stuff, aren’t we stealing it back?” 

“Are you some kind of Paladin of Torm?” the guard spat out. Vukardin is shocked, “But that makes us complicit in banditry\! Surely the guards of Neverwinter would never condone such a thing?” 

The guard sighs, “You aren’t going to make a lot of money doing this adventuring thing with that attitude.” But the comment insulted his professional pride, so he explains, “Lord Neverember has decided to establish the law of Neverwinter in the hinterland. But to do that, those opposing him must be dealt with. He's decided to use adventurers because he can’t bring a real army. Once the adventurers have pacified the area, we will arrive and establish order and the proper laws. It’s a process.” 

Vukradin muttered, “That seems very dangerous.” 

The guard’s eyes sparkled, ““If you are so concerned, bring it to the Wintershield headquarters. There you can give it to the Wintershield guards, and we will hold it for 60 days, and after the 60 days, if nobody claims it, we will take a portion for our retirement fund and you can keep the rest, secure in your knowledge that the real owners are no longer around to claim it.” 

His thoughts are disrupted when a client screams, “PLAY MUSIC BARD\!” Vukardin sighs, and begins playing a song that he was told might make him a penny. 

But he’s had enough, “I quit.” 

As he walks out, Brewbarry follows him, “You go and play music elsewhere?” 

Vukardin stares at Brewbarry, “I am going on an adventure to make some money to make music. You can help me. We won’t be part of this egregious money laundering scheme that the city of Neverwinter seems to be encouraging. Our goal is to make honest coin.” 

“You play music?”

Vukardin smiles, “Yes.” 

### Valphine Sortorra 

Valphine saw the Aasimar walk out of the bar and decided to follow him. She is a drow and a follower of Lathander. She is a paradox. 

The madness of the Underdark and the stories of Menzoberanzan's final fall led her to flee to the Overbrite. She had been told so many stories of the sun's evil, but when she saw it, it was a religious experience—something so powerful that it burned out the darkness that covered the skies. That was power. 

She stumbled on a cleric of Lathander who told her of the Morning God’s power, and she became a devoted follower of the god. 

She admired how the clerics on the one hand tried to pretend that they were humble, and on the other hand, used her to advance their gods’ presence and power. As a former follower of Lolth, she saw the duplicity as reassuring. 

However, she soon learned that the use of violence, scheming, and assassination was frowned upon. Her proposals were met with lectures about “How this is not the way.” 

She thought it was just a subterfuge, a scheme encouraging her to take action and not get caught. Drow society was all about rewarding successful schemes and punishing unsuccessful ones. But she soon found out that the clerics of Lathander did mean that the murder of enemies was wrong. 

“Except when it comes to killing monsters.” 

She smiled, “Monsters are what we call things we are allowed to kill.” And she remembered how many in Neverwinter thought she was a monster. 

As she drank in the First Flophouse, the bizarre combination of her clerical symbol and her race created space, and she could not stop staring at the Aasimar Vukardin. “A symbol of good. A symbol of the celestials.”

His music made no sense, but she could sense something about him. And when he stopped playing and told the barbarian that they would adventure, she had to follow. 

“I can help. I am a cleric of Lathander, and I, too, wish to adventure.” 

The bard stared at him and then nodded. 

Just outside the city limits, as they headed south, they encountered a tortle named Soma, a druid of Mieliki, who offered to guide them to Phandalin. 

“I know this land very well, and we will not go hungry.”  

## 8/1 of Taraksh 1495

### Soma 

The journey to Phandalin was uneventful, if long. Since the end of the barbarian incursion, the High Road was safe. And the Triboar Trail was less secure, but if you looked tough, or broke, or a bit of both, one could avoid trouble. 

Soma had made this journey several times and knew how to pull that off. The road to Phandalin was the only dangerous part of the journey. But she had heard rumors of a white dragon, discouraging bandits from attacking in open areas. A rumor that she kept to herself.

And soon they arrived at the mining town of Phandalin nestled in the snow-capped Sword Mountains. 

Soma turns to her companions, “This town consists of forty or fifty simple log buildings. Crumbling stone ruins surround the newer houses and shops.” 

Vukardin looks at it: " Are there no natural defenses for this town? No walls, rivers, anything?”

Soma shrugs, “There was a bigger town here that was destroyed centuries ago.” 

“And what of the people?” the bard asks her.

“Oh, they are quiet, hard-working folk who came from distant cities to eke out a life amid the harsh wilderness. They are farmers, stonecutters, blacksmiths, traders, prospectors, and children. The town has no walls or garrison, but most adults keep weapons within easy reach if they need to fight.”

She pauses, “ Visitors are welcome here, particularly if they have coin to spend or news to share. The Stonehill Inn at the center of town offers modest lodging and meals. A couple of doors down from the inn, posted outside the townmaster’s hall, is a job board for adventurers.”

Soma pulls out a map and says, " Here’s a map of the town with all the important stores marked.” 

Vukardin asks if the local Lionshield Coster has all the goods they once had. Soma shakes her head and repeats the rumors that the interdimensional supply chain has been disrupted somehow. 

“They are now forced to rely on the same kind of suppliers that the rest of the market has to.” 

### Vukardin

“Let’s get some food.” 

Vukardin leads the group to the Stonehill Inn, a modest, two-story roadhouse. 

Once inside, he meets the proprietor, a short, friendly male human named Toblen Stonehill. Toblen is a native of Triboar to the east who came to Phandalin to prospect, but soon realized that he knew much more about running an inn than he did about mining.

Vukardin has no coin, so the Bard convinces him to let his music pay for their meals. 

“As long as it's something popular from Waterdeep or Neverwinter.” 

Vukardin sighs, and plays.

As he finishes the third or fourth song, Toblen approaches Vukardin and asks him to play a song that the bard wants to. 

Vukardin is delighted, and the innkeeper seems pleased, so he gives him a complimentary glass of beer. 

And then mutters, “Once again, the Orcs have come down from the mountains to prey on the lowlands\! If Neverwinter doesn’t send help soon, the Orcs will overrun Phandalin and destroy everything we’ve worked so hard to rebuild. I am so pleased that you have come to help us.” 

Vukardin sputters, “So we get paid?”

Toblen looks at him, “Oh no. You go adventuring and take what you can from the monsters.” 

“But when did these Orcs raid?” 

“Years ago. The biggest threat we have had is from the Barbarian hordes.” And then Vukardin realizes the uncomfortable truth that Brewbarry is wearing the distinct tattoos of one of the tribes. He is momentarily worried, but Brewbarry mutters, “I like Vukardin music. My tribe goes boom, boom, boom with a drum. I don’t like drums. I like Vukardin.” 

To Vukardin’s relief, Toblen smiles, “Well, my friend, the wars of the past are the past.”   

“So will you be staying the night?” asks the innkeeper. 

“If it’s free?” 

“No, it’s not. So you should check out the quest board. That’s where the  townmaster has posted the jobs that pay.” 

Vukardin gets up, and as he packs his musical instruments, the Innkeeper says quietly, “Be careful, there is a rumor of a white dragon in the neighborhood.” 

“A WHITE DRAGON?” 

The Dwarven Prospectors

## 8/1 of Taraksh 1495

### Valphine Sortorra

The townmaster’s hall has sturdy stone walls, a pitched wooden roof, and a bell tower at the back. The job board next to the front door features a sparse number of notices, all written in Common and in the same hand.

Valphine knocks on the door, and a tremulous voice shouts, “If you’re a dragon, know that I'm far too thin and bony to make a good meal\!”

She looks at the house and thinks that the townmaster is a fool if he thinks this building will protect him. 

Vukardin reads the first quest out loud, “Dwarven Excavation Quest: Dwarf prospectors found ancient dwarven ruins in the mountains southwest of here, and have been working an archaeological dig seeking treasure and relics. They need to be warned that a white dragon has moved into the area. Take the warning to them, then return to Townmaster Harbin Wester to collect a reward of 50 gp.” 

Valphine asks the man in the building, “Are you Townmaster Harbin Wester? And do these quests pay as you said?” 

The voice clears its throat, “Yes\!” 

Vukardin shouts, “50 gold? To just deliver a message? I am so up for that\!” 

Soma mutters, “What about the next one?” 

“Gnomengard Quest: A clan of reclusive rock gnomes resides in a small network of caves in the mountains to the southeast. The gnomes of Gnomengarde are known for their magical inventions, and they might have something with which to defeat the dragon. Get whatever you can from them. If you bring back something useful and don't want to keep it for yourselves, Townmaster Harbin Wester will pay you 50 gp for it” 

Vukardin then reads the last one out loud, “Umbrage Hill Quest. “The local midwife, an acolyte of Chauntea named Adabra Gwynn, lives by herself in a stone windmill on the side of a hill a few miles south of Phandalin. With dragon sightings becoming more common, it’s not safe for her to be alone. Urge Adabra to return to Phandalin. Once she’s safe, visit Townmaster Harbin Wester to claim a reward of 25 gp.”

Valphine is most interested in the Gnomengard Quest for the opportunity of plunder, and hopes that the Bard will pick that one. But his conviction that plunder is somehow wrong leads him to choose the Dwarven quest because it has the highest payout. She is tempted to argue, but remembers that the clerics of the Morninglord have told her that plundering is not the way.  

And so they travel to where some ancient ruins can be found. “Ancient ruins have treasure,” she thinks and smiles. 

After a long 15-mile hike through the hilly terrain surrounding the town of Phandalin, she arrives late in the day near the foothills of the Sword Mountains. Soma has found some game. As it is dark, and the food looks tasty, they decide to camp out and head up the next day. 

“I see no dragon,” she mutters. 

## 9/1 of Taraskh 1495

### Soma

After a long night’s sleep in her shell, Soma starts the journey to the canyon. Once there, she admires its rocky walls that rise to a height of eighty feet. At the canyon's end, a twenty-foot-high black stone wall has a broken gate carved into it, with one stone door hanging precariously by a hinge and the other door missing. Beyond this open gate, a ruined settlement lies in the shadow of a great mountain to the east. 

Valphine mutters, “Nobody is here. We can claim to give the message and return.” 

Soma looks at her, uncertain if she is serious.

But before she can make up her mind to object or not, Vukardin declares that that would be wrong. 

And he marches past the broken doors. 

Soma follows him. Inside is a settlement that an avalanche of rubble destroyed. She notices that the rubble that once buried the settlement has been hauled away, leaving the outlines of stone buildings visible as collapsed walls.

“Archaeologists,” she thinks. 

A stone well on the far side of the ruins is filled with rubble.

“They throw their dirt into whatever hole they can find. That well might have provided water.”

She looks around carefully and notices that the settlement has been thoroughly ransacked. 

“Grave robbers,” she thinks.

Further into the settlement, she notices a partially collapsed, ten-foot-high wall that separates a courtyard from the settlement west of it. Three heaps of rubble are piled high in this area. Hewn from the canyon’s back wall, a thirty-foot-high temple facade features steps rising to a stone platform. Cut into this facade is a ten-foot-high open doorway flanked by crumbling, life-sized granite statues of cloaked dwarves. Evil grins can be seen on their weatherworn faces.

“Whatever settlement this was, its gods were not good.” 

And as she mutters to herself, two dwarves appear. 

Vukardin steps forward, “You are in danger of a white dragon; you should leave.” 

Before Soma can react, Vukardin begins to walk out of the cave. 

He looks at her, “I gave the message, let’s go collect.” 

The two dwarves look disappointed, and one pipes up  

“Perhaps we can interest you in another job?” 

Soma looks at him curiously. 

“My name is Dazlyn Grayshard, and this is Norbus Ironrune. We are shield dwarf prospectors and business partners. While looking for gold in the mountains southwest of Phandalin, we decided to explore a nearby canyon and found evidence of an ancient dwarven settlement buried by an avalanche. We have spent several months clearing the rubble and scouring the ruins for treasure, but have found nothing of value so far.

Until now.  Behind the settlement, carved into the back wall of the canyon, is an old temple of Abbathor, the evil dwarven god of greed. During solar eclipses, Abbathor is appeased with sacrifices of blood and gemstones. We think that on one occasion, the god found the sacrifices of this temple’s priests lacking, so he caused an earthquake and avalanche that collapsed parts of the temple and buried the settlement. We tried to go deeper but saw something that scared us. If you are willing to go in and deal with it, we could split what we find.”

Vukardin seems concerned, “Are you grave robbers? Are you stealing stuff that rightfully belongs to someone else?” 

Soma interrupts him, “Let’s hear them out, there may be money here.” 

Dazlyn, seeing an opening, says, “We don’t have money, but we could give you these sending stones. They are worth a lot of money to the right person. “

Vukardin appears hesitant, and Soma wonders how to convince him, when Valphine steps in, “Sending stones would allow you to send your music between two locations.”

### Vukardin 

“The use of the sending stones would allow for some fascinating musical effects”, thinks the Bard. He wonders how he could use the effect in some of his more recent compositions to add a layer of depth he has found lacking. 

But then something bothers him: “I just want to be clear. Everything you find here, do you intend to return to the rightful owners?” 

“Of course\!” says the dwarf named Norbus. 

Vurkadin is satisfied with the answer. The opportunity to create musical pieces with the sending stones is too tempting. “And when you are starving, you take risks for your art,” he argues with the inner voice screaming run away. 

As he heads into the temple, Dazlyn mutters, “I think we saw some oozes in there, but I could be wrong.” 


Vurkardin steps through the temple entrance. Spikes hammered into the floor hold open two sets of double doors. A once-secret door to the north stands open, with a room beyond it having only rubble.

He inwardly gulps and mutters about the need for risks for the art, and is about to march into the temple itself. Valphine mutters, “There’s a secret door here.” 

Vukardin coughs, “Excellent\!” 

The secret door to the south leads to a passageway heading south. Like all the ceilings here, the ceiling is 10 feet high, and the floor is dust and dirt. There is no light besides the light sources they are bringing with them. 

The passageway continues for 10 feet, heads southeast for 40 feet, and ends in a hallway with two doors spaced 10 and thirty feet apart. The doorway to the north ends in a wall. 

Valphine mutters again, “A secret door.” 

But Vukardin wants to explore the other door.  Once past the door, he sees a partially collapsed room.  

Soma mutters, “This is a bizarre layout.” 

Vukardin agrees and starts to clear out the dirt, but as he does, rocks shift, and the sound worries him. 

Stepping back, he looks around the room. His eyes now catch a feature he had missed. There are several protruding blocks. The blocks act as defensive positions for someone to defend the hallway from someone coming from the direction of the rubble. 

Vukadrin, “This room was cut in half. There may be a way to get around here from the other side.”   
Valphine Sortorra 

Valphine wasn’t evil. No, that’s not what she was. She was a product of Drow society. And in Drow society, niceties like good and evil were a privilege. She was a survivor, and more importantly, she was alive.

And she had stayed alive because she understood that when you meet an orc, you don’t walk up to the orc and parley, unless your blade is against its throat.

But Vukradin had other plans. 

“I intend to parley.” 

Soma whistles something that Valphine can only interpret as “dumbass.”

Valphine listens in disbelief as Vukradin asks, “Why are you here? Do you need help? Are you hungry?” 

Vukradin turns to Soma, “I have met orcs before in Neverwinter. They listened to my music. I don’t think these are threatening.” 

Valphine stares at him and wonders if the Orcs of the Overbright are different from the Orcs of the Dark Realms. 

The bard picks up a clarinet and says, “The Orcs in Neverwinter loved this music.” 

The Drow watches as the bard gets thwacked. The Orc’s swing of the axe misses him entirely, and it reminds Valphine of a saying that the gods protect fools. 

Valphine watches as Soma shouts, “You’re a lucky kid\!” And then casts Thorn whip, dragging one of the Orcs on the bluffs 20’ above the party down to the ground.  The creature rolls down the hill and lands prone. The drow is annoyed that the orc avoids most of the falling damage. 

And she hears Vukradin fall to the ground, knocked to death’s door by another Orc that rushed him from the cliff. 

She stares at the bard, and is tempted to let him die, but remembers that Lathander loves all creatures. The Drow cleric of light sighs and heals the bard, muttering about fools. 

And then unleashes a raw blast of coruscating divine energy to lay low her enemy. The prone orc is slightly singed. 

Lathander is not very pleased. Valphine will have to pray harder. 

As she ponders this, Brewbarry charges with his halberd, striking the prone orc and the one right next to it.  She smiles when the prone orc moves to attack Brewbarry, and is cut in half by the backswing of the Halberd. 

As for her patient, Vukradin, he’s attacked again. And this time, he has the look of a creature that understands that he’s got to fight. He looks so gallant, and ineffectual as his first blade barely touches the orc, and the other flies through the air. 

And Valphine sighs as an orc again strikes down Vukradin, again.

As she ponders what to do, another orc drops dead from Soma’s poisonous spray. 

“Poison\!” Valphine thinks back to all those pleasant memories. 

She strikes with her blade at one of the Orcs. And misses. 

Fortunately for her, Brewbarry rages when he sees Vukradin go down again. And attacks the Orcs in a frenzy of bloodlust. 

The Orcs, seeing the halberd, choose to throw a javelin rather than get closer, exposing themselves to an attack. The javelin hits, but the rage of Brewbarry protects him.

Valphine is surrounded, and she can feel this battle slipping away. From the corner of her eye, she sees Soma cast ice knife, and the blade flies towards her. The last thing she remembers is the pleasure of the ice hitting her body, ripping the skin apart, and the blood flowing out. 

### Soma

“Shit.” 

Her attack knocked out her cleric, and the two orcs were unaffected. 

Brewbarry looks at her, and she looks at him, “So we aren’t a well-oiled machine yet.” 

Looking in disgust, she mutters, “I just met you guys on the road\!” 

And Brewbarry strikes the two remaining orcs down with his halberd and rushes to heal his musical mentor, Vukradin. 

Soma rushes to help Valphine. The Drow has an ecstatic smile on her face. Soma is worried, but decides to heal her. 

“We should spend another night here and head out in the morning.” 

The next morning, Soma and the party head out towards Phandelin. She looks at Brewbarry, who is carrying the Orcs’ axes, and smiles. 

She also thinks back on last night. Dazlyn and Norbus were very happy to see the Orcs dead. So delighted that they cooked a fine meal. She also remembers the weird music played by Vukradin. Music that the bard claims was his own. 

Soma, used to the sounds of the swamps near Neverwinter, didn’t know what to make of it. 

But she had a shell she could retreat into, and when she did that, she could block out any sound she didn’t like. 

## 10/1 of Taraskh 1495

### Vukradin 

The march back to Phandalin through the hilly terrain between the Sword Mountains and Phandalin was easy enough, giving him time to think. 

He wasn’t too pleased with his performance. It wasn’t his best work, but his near-death experience still shook him up. 

The two dwarves seemed happy enough with his original compositions, but he knew they would have preferred if he played some of the more popular stuff in Neverwinter. 

His reverie was interrupted when he heard an Ogre up ahead whistling. 

“Valphine, is this a fellow musician?” 

“I would think he is a slave. Ogres were slaves in Menzoberranzan.” 

“Should we free him?” 

Vukradin doesn’t notice her eyes looking confused as she says, “If that’s what you overbrighters do. We had a large number of enslaved people in Menzoberranzan. This one could have escaped from there. A lot of people fled the Dark Realms when the rampaging demons leveled the great city of the Drow.”

The bard nods his head and shouts, “Are you a musician?” 

Had Vukradin dedicated less time to the intricacies of musical composition and performance, and more to understanding the diverse inhabitants of the world around him, the perilous nature of Ogres would have become starkly apparent. These formidable creatures are driven by a fundamental and insatiable hunger, a primal need to consume that underpins their very existence. Furthermore, their disposition is inherently violent and unpredictable, making any interaction fraught with danger. Perhaps most significantly, a crucial piece of knowledge that eluded the musically absorbed Vukradin was the Ogres' profound aversion to music and the arts. This deep-seated repulsion would have undoubtedly shaped any encounter, likely transforming a potentially neutral situation into one of immediate hostility. Vukradin's singular focus on his artistic pursuits, therefore, left him dangerously ignorant of critical realities that could have far-reaching consequences. 

As the ogre charged at him, Vukradin overheard Soma mutter, “The kid is going to get us killed.” 

But what the ogre didn’t know is that Vukradin hated those who hated the arts; he points a finger at the creature, casts Starry Wisp, and a mote of light streaks from his hand, striking the ogre. 

The ogre is startled and emits a dim light. 

And as the startled ogre growls, the bard runs away. 

From his hideout, he watches as Brewbarry charges at the Ogre. The halberd misses, and the Ogre laughs and marches closer to strike with its club, but in so doing, the creature exposes himself to another attack, and the blow is devastating. 

The blow is bloody, but not a killing blow. Vukradin grits his teeth as he hears the sound of the impacting club on Brewbarry’s flesh. 

A moment later, Soma casts poison spray, and the Ogre chokes.  

Vukradin, hidden from sight, hears Valphine groan as the Ogre dodges her divine fire. 

As the ogre still lives, he steps away from his hiding hole, unleashes another starry wisp, and again hides. 

And then the battle is over. Vukradin emerges from his hiding hole and sees Brewbarry pulling his halberd from the corpse of the dead ogre. 

He watches as Soma searches the corpse and picks up something. He chooses to ignore what he sees. 

### Valphine Sortorra 

“Once again in Phandalin,” she thinks. 

Vukradin mutters, “Time to collect our honest wages.” 

The drow rolls her eyes, but wonders if the Aasimar was brought here by Lathander to show her a better way. Maybe there is power in this that she doesn’t realize. She must observe. 

The bard bangs on the locked door of the Townmaster’s hall. A few moments later, a quavering voice shouts, “If you are a dragon, know that I am too thin and bony and won’t make a good meal.” 

Valphine laughs when Soma observes, “Dragons don’t knock on doors.”

And yet, a moment later, Townmaster Harbin opens the door, “Wait, aren’t you the musician who played at the Stonehill Tavern?” 

The bard nods his head and demands payment for completing the quest. 

The Townmaster smiles, “Well done\! They are very charming people.” 

“Seemed like grave robbers.” 

“What? What do you mean?” 

The bard continues, “They were digging in a ruin for artifacts. I don’t think they intended to take the artifacts to a museum.”  

Harbin pauses, “His lordship guarantees every adventurer tax-free plunder\!” 

And Valphine sighs as he listens to Vukradin’s diatribe about how adventurers are glorified thugs and goons stealing without regard to what is right and what is wrong.

###  Valphine 

“The townmaster is very upset.” She wants to ask, but Vukradin has already left. 

“Let’s get rid of some of our loot,” she hears Soma say. And so they go to the local Lionshield Coster to sell the broken axes and the hide armor they took from the bodies of the orcs. 

Inside, Valphine meets  Linene Graywind, the master of this outpost. 

“You are alive?” 

Vukradin interjects, “I had a near-death experience. It’s new for me. Never had one before.” 

Valphine adds, “The pain was glorious\!” 

Linene smiles, “Well, its good to see you here. I want to assure you that although our preferred mode of transportation of goods has been impacted, we are still carrying a wide variety of goods and can be relied on for all of your adventuring needs.” 

Valphine is curious, “Have tariffs disrupted your trade?” 

“Yes, you could say that.” 

Vukradin sees an opening, “Can we help with anything? Do you need a shipment of goods protected?” 

Linene looks at him confused, ‘No, not really, but I did hear a rumor that strange magic pervades Neverwinter Wood, confounding navigators and obscuring the ancient ruins of bygone kingdoms lost in its depths.”  

Valphine is curious about what has affected Lionshield’s Coster’s fabled internal network. A network that had made them an unstoppable force in the realms. 

But that’s a mystery for another day. Their next stop is the Stonehill Inn. 

Toblen Stonehill, the proprietor, once again convinces Vukradin to play some music for his clientele. 

Valphine looks around at the locals and decides that they have nothing of interest to share with her. And just sits and enjoys the music. 

## 1/2 of Taraskh 1495

### Soma 

The next morning, Soma once again heads out into the wilderness, towards the gnomish outpost of Gnomengarde. “The job is simple enough”, she thinks, “go there, get something that might be useful against dragons. And if we don’t think it's useful, but the gnomes do, sell it to the Townmaster for fifty gold.” 

The journey towards Gnomengard in the Sword Mountains goes through broken hilly terrain to the south of Phandalin before going up into the mountains themselves. 

Journey to Gnomengard

The expedition destined for the subterranean halls of Gnomengard, nestled deep within the rugged Sword Mountains, commences with a trek across the fractured, undulating landscape situated to the south of the burgeoning settlement of Phandalin. This initial phase of the journey involves navigating a labyrinth of broken hilly terrain, characterized by uneven ground, scattered rocks, and sparse vegetation, a stark contrast to the more settled lands surrounding Phandalin. Travelers must exercise caution and maintain a sure footing as they traverse this transitional zone, which serves as a prelude to the more challenging ascent into the imposing peaks of the Sword Mountains themselves. The air here may carry the scent of pine and damp earth, and the sounds of scurrying wildlife and perhaps the distant calls of mountain birds might accompany the passage. This lower region, while not as precipitous as the higher elevations, presents its own set of obstacles, demanding resilience and careful navigation before the true ascent towards Gnomengard begins.

The climb up is slow, but Soma has a sense for this kind of journey and leads her group through a series of mountain paths. As she turns, the path emerges into a narrow valley with a 5-foot-wide path, surrounded by steep walls to either side. Ahead in the middle of the valley is an ogre. 

Vukradin asks, “Is this a slave?” 

And the drow shrugs and says, “When they were slaves, they didn’t whistle cheerfully.” 

Soma is about to object, but Vukradin is enraged, “So he just wants to kill us? Everyone wants to kill us\!” 

The Ogre shouts, “I'm hungry\!” 

Vukradin offers him some food, but the Ogre objects and points at Soma, “I want turtle\!” 

Soma is appalled and amused when Vukradin fails to intimidate the Ogre, and instead convinces the Ogre that these are easy pickings, and it shouts, “I'm hungry\! I eat Turtle\! I eat you\!”  

Soma shouts, “We killed your brother\!”  

The Ogre howls. 

Soma smiles, covers him in poison, and then rushes away. 

The Ogre charges at Brewbarry, who misses. The Ogre, in turn, misses the large barbarian. 

Valphine then uses one of the magical bullets Brewberry found on the last Ogre to knock it prone.

# Chapter 02 To find a shapeshifter

## 02-01 of Taraskh 1495 

### Valphine

“The ogre is prone on the ground under the sun. Like Lathander obliterates the darkness with his light, I will smash his body,” Valphine thinks, her muscles tensing, a grim determination set on her face. The morning sun, usually a source of warmth and comfort, now illuminates the brutish form of their downed foe, a testament to the battle that has raged through the early hours. She sees an opportunity, a chance to end this struggle decisively.

With a grunt of exertion, her mace swings through the air, a metallic arc against the backdrop of the rugged mountain peaks. The weighty weapon descends, intended to crush, to obliterate the ogre. But fate, or perhaps simply a moment of misjudgment, intervenes. The mace lands with a dull thud against the ogre's hide, a glancing blow that carries no force, no impact. The creature, surprisingly resilient, remains unhurt.

From her left, Valphine hears the unmistakable sound of Soma’s snigger, a quiet, mocking sound that grates on her nerves. “A broad side of a barn would have been harder to miss,” Soma jibes, her voice low but cutting, a constant irritant amidst the chaos of battle. Valphine’s jaw tightens, a flush of annoyance rising in her cheeks.

Then, from her right, she hears the roar of Brewbarry, a sound that promises devastation. The Uthgardt barbarian, a force of nature in his own right, swings his formidable halberd down on the ogre. The massive weapon slices through the air with a menacing whisper, a testament to Brewbarry’s strength and fury. But just like Valphine’s strike, the blow misses its mark. The halberd, instead of finding purchase on the ogre’s flesh, strikes the rocky ground with a deafening clang that echoes through the tight mountain valley. The sound resonates, a stark reminder of their collective failure to land a decisive blow.

Just in front of her, a puff of green gas, acrid and foul, suddenly surrounds the ogre. It coughs, a guttural sound that speaks of pain and discomfort. The gas, evidently a potent concoction from one of their more magically inclined companions, has found its mark. The creature is hurt, its movements momentarily hampered, but it is not felled.

With a surprising burst of energy, the ogre stands, its beady eyes scanning the faces of its attackers. It looks at Valphine, then at Brewbarry, its monstrous mind weighing its options, deciding who to strike next. A moment of chilling deliberation, and then its gaze settles on the towering barbarian. It picks the Uthgardtian.

Valphine watches in a moment of suspended horror as the ogre’s crude, but massive, axe lands on Brewbarry. A sickening thud, and for a minute, the barbarian buckles, his enormous frame swaying. But then, a miracle. Thanks to the legendary rage of the Uthgardt barbarian and his mystical powers, the axe does nothing. The blow, intended to cleave him in two, glances off his hardened skin, absorbed by an invisible resilience.

The failure of such a mighty blow catches both the Ogre and Valphine by surprise. Valphine, her own heart pounding, watches the creature stare in disbelief, its brutish face contorted in a mix of confusion and fear. And then, a truly astonishing sight: the ogre turns and runs, its powerful legs carrying it away from the fight, its previous aggression replaced by a primal instinct for self-preservation.

Valphine, her mind still reeling from the unexpected turn of events, swiftly puts an arrow in her handheld crossbow. Her movements are practiced, instinctual. She aims at the fleeing creature, a dark silhouette against the sun-drenched mountainside, and shoots. The bolt whistles through the air, finding its mark. The beast is wounded, a fresh spurt of blood staining its hide, but it continues to run, its speed undiminished. Even Brewbarry, his fury still simmering, cannot bring him down.

“Vukradin does the killing blow,” Valphine thinks, as she watches the ogre breathe its last. A quiet satisfaction settles over her, a sense of accomplishment despite the messy end to the encounter.

And from the rear, she hears Soma shout to Vukradin, her voice laced with indignation, “He was running away\! This was senseless.” Soma, ever the pragmatist, sees only the unnecessary expenditure of effort, the pursuit of a defeated foe.

Valphine is surprised by Vukradin’s answer, a calm, almost philosophical response that seems out of place in the aftermath of battle. “He hated music,” Vukradin states, his voice even. “And he probably had some treasure he had stolen from someone else.” A shrug, a simple justification for an act that, to Soma, seemed utterly pointless. The battle may be over, but the quirks and motivations of her companions continue to surprise Valphine.

Valphine looks over the body and finds a whistle, some coins, and a key. 

### Soma

The rest of the journey to Gnomengarde is uneventful. Soma finds the river that leads to the gnomish hold. At the end of the river is a waterfall whose erosion of the rock has created a natural concavity. The roaring waterfall creates a cloud of mist as it plunges into a shallow pool of water, within which rise two small islands covered with two-foot-tall red, green, and purple mushrooms. Several cave openings overlook the pool from rocky ledges twenty to thirty feet above. The mountain blocks any sunlight from reaching this place. 

“Where to?” 

And before she can answer, Vukradin is wading through the water towards the mushrooms. She follows him closely. 

The mushrooms are two feet tall and grow atop small islands in the middle of the 3-foot pool. 

Soma watches Vukradin as he examines them. 

“These red ones are oily. Not sure what they are useful for. These Green ones remind me of a mushroom that can be turned into flour. We should forage as many as we can. And these purple mushrooms can be fermented to make mushroom wine.”

Some has a delighted expression on her face as she imagines what it tastes like, “I want some of those.”  

Vukradin doesn’t understand her expression and assumes she is jesting and says, “Mushroom wine tastes as bad as it sounds.” 

Soma shrugs.

With the mushrooms in his bag, Vukradin shouts, “Let’s go find the secret treasure room behind the waterfall.”

Soma stares at him. He announces, “There is always a secret treasure room behind the waterfall.”

She follows him and stands under the waterfall, getting soaked. And behind the waterfall is nothing but a rock wall. Vukradin taps at the rock, touches the rock, and pokes at the rock, but it is \- just that \- rock. 

“Can we get out of here?” she asks. 

Vukradin nods. He looks at the cliff wall next to the waterfall, and notices that there is an entrance 20 feet above. 

He starts to climb up. 

Soma shrugs, and follows him. 

Valphine and Brewbarry stand and watch. 

The druid shouts, “You coming?” 

“No,” answers the Drow. 

Soma looks at her and sighs. The Drow wants a rope. So the druid climbs down, takes the rope from the Drow's hands, and climbs up again. 

Once up the 20’ cliff, Soma walks up stairs that lead 15 feet deeper into the mountain and open up into a rough chamber with a hallway to the north, east, and a slick rock wall to the south, atop which is a guard post. 

A gnome shouts in Gnomish. Soma stares at him. Then another female voice shouts, “Who goes there?”

Vukradin answers, “Vukradin, the Bard\!” 

The gnome asks, “Are you a shapechanger?” 

“No.”  

“Can you prove it?” 

Soma grouses, “Would we take these shapes if we were shapechangers?” 

The female gnome talks to the male gnome and then says, “That’s what a shapechanger would say\!” 

Soma rolls her shoulders, and mutters, “I sense more senseless violence coming.” 

But Vukradin isn’t done. 

“Your standing orders are only to attack shape changers; your interpretation would lead to attacking anyone. Is that the intent of the orders?” 

The male gnome looks at Vukradin, and the female gnome shouts, “Perhaps, but that’s what a shapechanger would say.” 

Brewbarry has had enough. “I am Brewbarry, killer of Ogres\! I am no shapeshifter\!” 

The male gnome and the female gnome talk some more. The female gnome announces, “We’ve decided that he’s a Uthgardt Barbarian and not a shapeshifter.” 

Brewbarry growls, “I used to be one.” 

At that, the female gnome smiles, “Oh, that’s so much better. There used to be a standing order to attack Uthgardtians on sight as a result of the events of the last few months. But since you used to be one, it’s unclear whether that standing order stands. Furthermore, at the last meeting, it was unclear if the ‘attack uthgardian barbarians’ order was renewed and so given that we have decided to let you pass.” 

Soma stares in disbelief, “Bureaucracy saved us.” 

### Vukradin

“I want to learn more about our new friends. Tell me, friends, who are you? Do you like music? I am a bard.”

The male gnome shouts, “Pog,” and the female gnome shouts, “I am ulla\! And yea, we like music. Mostly gnomish music.” 

Vukradin tries a few notes, and the gnomes seem pleased. 

Pog waves his hand, as if to tell Vukradin to stop, and asks, “Why are you here?” 

Vukradin explains that the mayor is looking for some kind of magical device that can help fight against the threat of the dragon. 

Ulla scratches her head and says, “You should go to the inventor workshop.” She tells Vukradin that the best way to get there is to cross the hanging bridge from where they entered the caves. 

Vukradin thanks them and marches towards the inventor’s workshop. After crossing the bridge, he enters a room that is lightly obscured by the mist of the waterfall. But he notices, just in time, that the room contains two rapidly spinning devices that look like turnstiles fitted with stacks of long, sharp blades spaced 1 foot apart. The northern turnstile spins counterclockwise, while the southern one spins clockwise.

He stares in disbelief and marches back to the where Pug and Ulla were sitting. 

“That was a death trap\!” 

Ulla is surprised. “I thought you had a mage who could cast Mage Hand. Well if you don’t, then you’ll have to go the long way through the northern hallway. Go north past the first passageway going east, past a large room, and then you’ll see another passageway going east out of the mountain. Go out from there. Then cross the river, and climb up the cliff wall, where you will enter the sleeping chambers of most of the gnomes. From there, there is a passageway going south that leads to the inventors’ workshop.” 

Vukradin thanks her and heads north. 

The first large room is not empty. It has a rotating platform equipped with four heavy crossbows that reload automatically. The inventor is a deranged gnome, as they learn later, named Facktore, who decides to test his device on Vukradin and his companions. 

Although Vukradin is tempted to kill him, he decides that perhaps disarming the device is sufficient. 

With the bow disabled and Facktore having fled the scene of the battle, Vukradin climbs down the cliff wall, wades through the river, stopping on the island of mushrooms to pick a few more, and then climbs the cliff wall again. 

Once he’s climbed the walls, he enters a large cave that is strewn with the remnants of old campfires. Four side caves serve as sleeping areas, with five small wooden cots crammed into each one. 

To the south is the entrance to the laboratory of the gnomes. 

### Valphine

The Drow cleric stares at the two gnomes arguing. She is familiar with these debates among inventors, arguing over details that don’t matter. 

Vukradin explains that they are there to look for help to fight a dragon, and the inventors brush him off. 

“That’s unimportant compared to the calamity facing our community. My name is Fibblestib, and this is my coworker, Dabbledob. We are Gnomengarde’s foremost inventors, and we are entirely focused on a cure for King Korboz’s madness.” 

Dabbledob looks at him and grouses, “If you think your proposal will do anything you’re a fool. There is no evidence that any such ray would work.” 

She turns to Valphine, “A sanity ray\!” 

Fibblestib is offended and immediately starts shouting, “You want to build a straitjacket instead. A jacket with no holes for the hands\! That’s not a straitjacket, that’s a shirt with no holes for the hands.” 

Before Valphine can interrupt them, Dabbledob and Fiddlestib argue some more amongst themselves. 

Valphine looks at them, “I am a cleric\!” 

Both gnomes stare at her aghast, “We are gnomes, we invent our way out of illness.” 

Soma tries to explain the value of cleric spells, but the gnomes just keep shouting louder. 

Valphine turns to Vukradin, “I don’t think I could cure him, and I also don’t think we have the money.” 

Vukradin counts the money in his head and sighs, “Yes.” 

Fiddlestib turns to Valphine, “I think we should walk you through what happened. It will allow us to revisit all of the salient facts. And please interrupt us with any questions\! You may see something that we missed.” 

And so the two inventors explain that two gnomes, Warren and Orrin, went missing and that King Korboz claims it was a shape-changing creature. 

Valphine hears what they have to say, and before she can suggest torture, Brewbarry says, “We talk\! We cure\!”

She smiles, the barbarian and she are on the same wavelength. Torture is what purifies the crazed mind. 

But before she can make the case, Vukradin starts talking again and explains that he would like to try music. 

Dabbledob sighs, “Music has helped in some circumstances.” 

Vukradin asks if they have a piano, and Fiddelstib regretfully says no, but offers to build one. “It won’t be a normal piano\! But it will play music.” 

### Vukradin

“Let’s go talk to the king.” 

Vukradin is not interested in arriving at any new death traps, and asks for the safest way to the throne room. 

Vukradin explains what happened with the rotating blades and the rotating crossbow assault system.

Fiddelstib laughs. 

The gnome inventor adds, “My invention, the rotating blades, is the better option. And you have proven it.” 

Vukradin notices how Dabbledob rolls her eyes. 

A few moments later, Vukradin is at the door to the King’s room.  

The King is in a state of hysterics, screaming. Another voice, his co-King Gnercli shouts, “Who is that?” 

“Vukradin\!” 

King Korboz shouts, “A shapeshifter\!” 

The co-King sighs, “I am King Gnercli. Are you adventurers?” 

“We are on a diplomatic mission from Townmaster Harbin Wester to acquire a device to fight the dragon with.” 

King Gnercli sighs, “You sound like adventurers. How about this, kill the shapeshifter, and I will give you a device.” 

Vurkadin mutters, “I am a musician.” 

And he laughs when Soma adds, “More of a tour guide.” 

King Gnercli sighs again, “Look, there is some kind of creature that is terrorizing our cave system. Can you deal with it or not?” 

Vukradin groans, “Where are we supposed to find this thing?” 

“Well, it’s not bipedal. So if I had to guess, it would hide in a place with a lot of big things it could shape shift into.”

The King pauses, “The cellar. There are a lot of barrels.” 

Vukradin asks, “And what treasure will you give us?” 

“A hat of wizardry\!” 

Vukradin shouts, “Not exactly going to terrorize a dragon with that.”

King Gnercli shouts, “I don’t have much else.” 

Soma then reminds Vukradin that they get the money for bringing something, not necessarily for bringing something helpful.

Vukradin ponders the distasteful nature of such a deal, counts the 50 gold in his head, and sighs, “deal.” 

The bard and his friends go through the room with the spinning blades, this time disabling the blades , then cross the bridge, and arrive where Pog and Ulla are sitting. 

###  Valphine

Valphine, who knows about more dangerous shapeshifters in the Dark Realms, stares at the two gnomes, convinced they must be the shapeshifters. 

Ulla looks disturbed and shouts, “We are real gnomes\!” 

Valphine shouts, “That’s what a shapeshifter would say\!” 

Ulla turns on Pug, “I noticed how he looked a little bit different the past few days\!” 

Pug turns on Ulla, “Me? You’ve looked different.” 

The two continue to argue in front of the Drow, who smiles. 

From there, she follows the passage north, and instead of going to the room where they found the rotating crossbow, she takes a right into a room full of barrels. 

This room contains twelve forty-gallon barrels set into wide alcoves. A wooden brace secures each barrel. The barrels in the south alcove have been tapped with wooden spigots. Two of those barrels are half full, and two are nearly empty.

She steps into the room and points a crossbow at the first barrel. 

And the barrel immediately transforms into a mimic, its pseudo-pods reaching out to strike, and its massive mouth full of razor-sharp teeth opens. 

“We found it\!” shouts Valphine

Brewbarry charges at the creature, striking with his Halberd. The beast is wounded, but the weapon is stuck in the creature’s body. 

Valphine sees Soma prepare to cast Ice Knife and makes sure she is out of range of the clumsy druid’s spell. 

The mimic advances on Brewbarry, attacks with a pseudo that misses the barbarian entirely. 

The bard unleashes invectives, and at first, Valphine is confused but sees the underlying enchantment that causes the mimic to flinch visibly. 

She smiles and repeats a rhyme she remembers from her youth, “Sticks and stones may break my bones, and words can also hurt me.”

# Chapter 03 The Bard, the Kings, and the Carver

## 02-01  of Tarkash 1495 

###  Vukradin 

Vukradin, ever the theatrical one, taunts the grotesque creature before them. “We have it outnumbered\! It’s stunned\! We shall kill it before it lays a hand on us\!” His voice booms, filled with an almost reckless confidence that, at times, borders on delusion.

But the battle is not going as planned. Brewbarry, the stalwart warrior, struggles in vain to pull his halberd free, the weapon seemingly stuck fast in some unseen impediment. Soma's usually potent puff of poison, a sickly green cloud that had felled countless foes, dissipates harmlessly around the creature, leaving it utterly unaffected. Even the nimble mimic, usually so precise, misses its strike at Brewbarry, its attack sailing wide.

“You will not touch us\!” Vukradin declares, attempting to weave another of his magical incantations, a spell he’d once described as ‘utterly foolproof’ for its ability to deter. But this time, the mimic, with an unnerving flicker in its multifaceted eyes, seems wise to his magical words. It remains utterly unaffected, its alien intelligence seemingly having adapted to his parlor tricks.

At this point, Soma, usually reserved and focused on the immediate threat, mutters under her breath, a rare show of frustration. “Unnatural magical creations that have no place in the material world.”

Vukradin, with his usual impeccable timing for tangential conversations, turns to her, a glint of curiosity in his eyes. “Wait, you’re a naturalist druid?”

Soma looks at him, her expression a mix of disbelief and annoyance that he would choose this precise moment, mid-battle, to discuss theological taxonomy. “Yes,” she replies, her voice clipped. “Constructs, extra-planar creatures, are all abominations. Disruptions to the natural order.”

Vukradin, unable to resist, presses on, a mischievous glint in his eye. “What about Aasimar’s and Tieflings?” He pronounces the words with a dramatic flourish, clearly relishing the debate.

Soma looks at him, truly confused this time. “What are those?” she asks, her brow furrowed. The question, delivered with genuine ignorance, clearly takes Vukradin by surprise.

Vukradin, momentarily flustered, mutters, “Aasimar are touched by Celestials, Tieflings by the Abyss\!” He gestures vaguely upwards and then downwards, as if sketching the celestial and infernal realms in the air.

Soma, however, remains unimpressed by his poetic flair. She looks at him with a steady, pragmatic gaze. “You’re just another creature born into this world,” she states, her voice calm and unwavering. “There is no celestial touching here.”

Vukradin’s face contorts in annoyance. His poetic license, a cornerstone of his self-proclaimed identity, had been challenged. “I am a poet,” he declares, his voice rising in indignation, “and I get to take whatever poetic license I want. And I will not have you deny my allusion.”

Meanwhile, oblivious to the philosophical debate raging behind him, Brewbarry is about to unleash a powerful, albeit desperate, punch with his bare fists when Vukradin, ever observant despite his theatricality, asks, “You have no ranged weapons.”

Brewbarry, realizing his oversight, thumps his head with a meaty hand, a moment of exasperated self-reprimand, and then, from some hidden pouch, pulls out a pair of gleaming handaxes.

And then, with a final, decisive strike, Soma finishes it off, her earlier philosophical musings giving way to efficient, deadly action. The unnatural creature, a temporary blight on the material world, is no more.

## Soma 

“Let’s see what else is here,” I muttered.

And on cue, I heard Vukradin question my choices, “You are going to steal gold?”

I wanted to hide inside my shell. “If you want to live the impoverished life, that’s your choice. I am not opposed to some gold of questionable provenance.”

And I pointedly turned my back on him.

But I was out of luck; he wasn’t done with me. “I am rich\! I have sending stones\!”

And thankfully, Valphine continued talking to him, “But I thought you were going to use them as part of your music?”

“No, they can only be used for a single short message.”

I remembered a particular bird in the forest that would sing a single note all season, and how everyone would wait for this note, and wondered whether I should tell Vukradin this. And I remembered that I hadn’t been paid, and decided not to.

After scouring the room with the chests and finding nothing the gnomes forgot, I followed Vukradin to the inventors, where Fiddlestib and Dabblebob were very excited to see us.

I handed them over the proof of the monster's death, and before I could stop them, they started discussing what kind of construct they could create from the creature's entrails.

“This is how the abominations that walk the north came to be. Inventors who showed no concern for the natural world.”

But I kept my mouth shut.

And followed Vukradin to the King’s room, where we were to receive our prize.

### Valphine

I watch as Vukradin attempts to negotiate with the two Kings. And I sigh.

King Korboz complains that King Gnercli “Doesn’t listen to him and believe a single word he has to say.”

And I am about to cut their heads off when Vukradin begins to amuse me.

“I find it rude that you didn’t believe your king.”

At which point Gnercli shouts, “I am the king.”

Vukradin asks, blandly, “So how do you make decisions?”

“We work together,” explains Gnercli, his voice tense.

I stifle a laugh.

“And when you disagree? There is no decision?”

I can sense the tension, “Celestial? He sounds more like a Tiefling.”

Gnercli explains, “This is a dual monarchy, not a single monarchy. So we argue until a decision is made.”

I can barely keep it together; this is too ridiculous.

Vukradin won’t stop. “How do you decide who wins?”

“The best argument wins,” insists Gnercli.

“And who decided which is best?”

King Korboz, who has recovered from his fear, explains, “Together.”

I now have to insert myself: “You need a clear approver structure.” I have seen cultures like these and have enjoyed tearing them apart. They pretend to be a commune, but have more betrayals, violence, and politics than even the Drow Noble Houses.

Will Vukradin explode their happy commune?

And he does, “I’m wondering if you had three kings, wouldn’t it become more difficult?”

At which point Gnercli cuts him off, “We have two kings because we do not believe in the despotic autocratic decision making of a single individual who could be rendered unfit for leadership because of a shapeshifter.“

And then Korboz shouts, “That you didn’t believe existed\!”

I wonder where the Bard is going with this, and he twists the knife expertly, “So if you need a new king to have two, what happens?”

“Well, we elect another.”

“So one is the younger king and the other is the older and wiser king?”

King Gnercli, obviously annoyed, says, “There is no seniority\!”

“So let me get this straight, if I have been King for a decade, and this new guy becomes King, I have to treat him as an equal and take orders from him?”

King Gnercli mutters, “Where did you learn all this about government?”

And I smile as the Bard spins a tale of his expertise and training, fictional no doubt.

And on cue, King Korboz shouts, “I told you as the senior king I should have preferential treatment\!”

And at that point, I smile. The two kings will be at each other's throats for months if not years.

Vukradin cuts them off, “You said there was a magical hat for us?”

King Gnercli, angry at Vukradin, shouts, “Here\! And go\!”

As I walk past the two inventors, I realize that they have been overhearing us.

Fiddlestib tells Vukradin, “I am in favor of a bicameral legislature with a unitary executive\!”

Dabbledob, trying to one-up her, explains, “I prefer more kings\! That way we could have a vote\!”

Vukradin tries to create more chaos, like a good Drow, and says, “I think you should be king\!”

But the two inventors are more interested in building a tamper-proof voting box. Or rather, arguing over whether such a thing is possible.

### Soma

The tortle is pleased that she is a guide for Vukradin. His tab continues to grow, and at some point, she will want to be paid, but she is fine for now. 

Arriving in Phandalin, she leads him to the Townmaster, who again insists he is a tasteless morsel for a dragon.  

With the fifty gold in their pockets, split four ways, and the sun setting, she heads off to spend the night in the Stonehill Tavern. 

Surprisingly, the Bard performs well. And then Soma learns about a curious tale that she had heard rumors about. 

“There was a play in Triboar. It had as its main actor someone who was always dressed in character as a Demon, but had the most ridiculous name, Bob. His performances were legendary\! And your performance reminded me of that.” 

The Bard perks up, for he, too, had heard of this play. It had had a spectacular run several years ago, although it ended. He had been trying for years to get the script. He shouts, “Perhaps we can do a revival\!” 

The tavern keeper looks at him, “I am not sure where you would go to find the script, but Triboar is as good a place as any.” 

## 03-01  of Taraskh 1495 

### Valphine

I was annoyed. We were going to save a woman’s life, at our risk, for a mere 25 gold. It seemed absurd. But Lathander’s Cleric had cautioned me about this.

But then Vukradin, once again, surprised me, “I think we should ask for more than 25 gold. This seems like too little money.”

My interest was piqued; did the others agree with me?

Soma, who cares about all life, disagreed, of course.

But Vukradin muttered, “But my studio is going to take forever to build at this rate.”

I rolled my eyes. This fool could solve all of his problems if he would just do what we are allowed to \- take gold from monsters, also known as creatures that Lord Nevermber thinks don’t belong in his territory.

Soma, again, tried to thwart his natural impulses when she said, “Sometimes the reward is knowing you did the right thing.”

When Vukradin dismissed her, she muttered, “I just have a kinship with life. I don’t want anyone to die.”

I heard that and almost coughed, as I thought of her Ice Knife. The Tortle explained that 25 gold was plenty.

I stared in disbelief at the Tortle, who continued, “I don’t want a new studio. Just a nice new teapot.”

And so the talking continued as we made our way to Umbrage Hill to save Adabra.

*Some time later.* 

The chill wind bites at my face as I pick my way carefully along the narrow trail winding through the rocky hills. The fading light casts long shadows over the jagged stones and scraggly bushes, and the silence feels heavy, too heavy. I grip my sword tightly, senses straining for any sign of movement.

Then, out of the corner of my eye, I catch a flicker—a shadow slipping behind a boulder—my heart hammers.

But I dismiss this.

I am not in the Dark Realms, worried about every shadow. 

### Soma 

Bandits. Yes, the noise is bandits. Valphine had this tense look on her face, but said nothing. Maybe she sensed something? Perhaps she didn’t. But these bandits would have gotten the jump on us if they had not made so much noise. 

Vukradin shouts that we’re going to die. 

I can sense his fear. I am old, and I have seen much, and I am not going to die today.  

And then I am shaped like a spider. This new power of mine is quite strange. I can think and feel as myself, and I am also wholly spider. 

With spider-like ease, I quickly climb up and strike my enemy. 

Through my many eyes, I can see him strike with a scimitar and miss. 

I take a glance behind me, down below, where the rest of my group is. A bandit aims at Valphine. She’s hit. 

To my right, I see the Barbarian take note of a bandit on a hill. Like Brewbarry has done for so many years in the wild, he climbs up and then swings his halberd. The blade slices the air, and at first I think that he’s missed, and then the head of the bandit flies off. The body falls towards Brewbarry, who is now covered in blood. 

Why isn’t Vukradin doing anything? Oh, right, he’s in shock. They are so young.

But this bandit is going to die here today. And her bite release crushes his hand, and the poison leaves her glands. 

The bandit dies. 

All life is precious, but not a bandit who is trying to kill me. 

I turn around to see what to kill next. 

One of the bandits takes out his crossbow, misses, and starts to run. He’s afraid. And he should be. 

And another bandit, seeing my form, runs screaming \- “Spiders\!\!\!\!” 

Vukradin screams at the one who attempted to hit Brewbarry, “Catch him\! He’s taking stolen treasure\!” 

And of course, the Drow reaches casually with her hand-held crossbow and strikes the fleeing bandit in the back. And a sprinting Vukradin kills him.  

We are assholes. 

And so I turn my head to that poor bandit who was afraid of spiders. And there is Brewbarry, covered in blood, sprinting to get next to him. 

“Let him go\!” I shout. But realize I am speaking like a Spider. And wonder, what does that sound like? 

I sit down. 

### Brewbarry 

My rage consumes me. And yet, there is something about this man’s fear. And I think that he has lost his tribe. And I feel sadness. 

I drop my halberd and shout, “Friends.” 

He looks at me, and I can tell that he has suffered at the hands of my people. 

“I am so sorry that the Uthgardts hurt you. They were mean to me, too.” 

The man stares at me, a look of confusion on his face. He was expecting to die, not get an apology.  

“They were mean to me, too.” 

The man stares and says, “They pillaged my village, destroyed everything.” He looks at me and sobs, “I had no money, nothing. I am not a bad person. I don’t want to steal things. It’s the Carver’s fault.”

### Vukradin 

The bandit has a boss. I must learn more. 

“You should join us at dinner and tell us about the Carver?” 

I stare at him, a bit of menace, a bit of kindliness. The form of an Aasimar can always be helpful. 

“What’s there to say. He’s the big boss. And he’s big. I’ve never met him. I just worked with Jax.” 

He looks at me like a puppy who has found its momma. I smile. And then he asks, “Can I be with you guys?”

I smile, “Of course.” 

### Soma

There’s a scroll. I pick it up. It has a druidic spell. 

And then I hear the annoying voice of Vukradin reminding me that this really should be returned to its rightful owner. 

I stare at him in disbelief, and then realize he has a point. 

Am I any better than a bandit if I keep this?

# Chapter 04 Saving Adabra

## 04-01 Taraskh 1495

### Vukradin 

Corbin stands before Vukradin. Corbin is a gaunt man in his late twenties, with the haunted, hollowed-out look of someone who has stared into the abyss and found it staring back. His hair is a matted, dirt-brown tangle, and a patchy, uncared-for beard clings to his jaw. His eyes, a pale blue, are often distant and unfocused, but can sharpen with a desperate, feral intensity when threatened. He wears ill-fitting leather armor scavenged from a dead man, and his movements are tinged with a weary resignation, punctuated by moments of nervous energy.

Vukradin thinks for a moment and is displeased, “Is that stolen armor?” 

The look on Corbin’s face is enough for Vukradin. He knows. 

Brewbarry pushes, “Vukradin asked you\!” 

Vukradin examines Corbin’s facial features, and the fear in Corbin’s eyes, and the doubt, and finally Corbin answers, “The owner was already dead?” 

The bard is outraged; this is why the world is such a mess. Taking the armor off the dead is the final act of treachery and thievery of a world gone mad. 

“I had no choice.” 

Vukradin notices the sweat on Corbin’s face. He stares impassively. 

“I was a bandit. And it was either wear this armor or wear nothing and die. I don’t want to die.” 

“Well, Corbin, working for us, you will be taking care of our camp. Therefore, no armor is required. Take it off,” commands Vukradin. 

“Mr Brewbarry, can I please keep my armor?” 

Vukradin inwardly sniggers as Brewbarry wears none. 

“I don’t wear any.” 

The despair on the bandit’s eyes upsets Vukradin and so he relents, “We need to get you some proper fair trade armor.” 

The bandit is relieved, sighs, and says,” Well, until then I will wear this to protect myself.” 

A spider suddenly squeaks, moves its arms frantically and points at Corbin as if it is trying to ask a question.

Corbin sees the spider and freaks out. 

Vukradin laughs, “That’s Soma, our tortle.’ 

### Soma  

This spider's body is fun. But I can’t communicate. I mean, I can, but only with other spiders. But seeing the world from this angle, with these eyes, teaches you so much about the natural world and the natural order. I smell things and see things and taste things that I didn’t know existed. It’s an explosion of senses. 

And no more. The time has passed and I am tortle again. 

The bandit is in shock. I look at him and say, “It is true I am tortle. And why do you need armor?” 

The bandit answers back, “Because I am human.” 

I look at his squishy form and think how it's strange that this race has dominated so much of Faerun.

And we continue our journey until we reach a hill, atop of which is a windmill, a set of cairns, and a ruined building. 

Atop the windmill is, quite obviously, a manticore. And soon I can hear the voice of a woman coming from the building, “Help me\!” 

I think about how best to advance but Valphine starts asking questions. 

“What do you do in the overbright when there’s people being attacked by monsters?

“She looks like she’s in need. We would usually try and save the sentient life.” 

Valphine turns to Vukradin and asks, “We were told to bring her back.” 

I know where this is going, “Yes. But it was implied alive.” 

“So we must kill the manticore?” 

And of course Vukradin has an angle, “What if we killed the Manticore, returned to Phandalin, demanded more money, and then came back and brought her to the village?”

I look at him and roll my eyes. “How about we just kill the manticore and save her?”  

And with that, we begin to climb up the hill quietly, trying to avoid drawing attention. 

Behind, I hear Corbin ask Vukradin, “Hey why don’t you leave your musical instrument here, so it won’t get damaged.” 

I want to laugh, but it would be too loud.  

“No.” 

The bandit has this look of terror on his face: “I just wanted to make sure it doesn’t get damaged.” 

He is a little child, lost, and I have to help. 

“Hey Vukradin, I can always cast mending.” 

Vukradin looks at me and says, “Thank you.” 

I stare at him, confused. 

“I am not the kind of musician who thinks that hands are better than magical tools.” 

I smile. The bard needs my help, and guidance. 

Vukradin turns to me, “Let’s go quietly.” He points to the manticore a distance away. I nod. 

And although Vukradin is silent, I am not. 

The manticore perks its head at us and can see us all.

I missed my chance to talk to it.  

### Valphine

The creature roars. I put one of the bolts in my hand crossbow, and target the creature. 

And of course Vukradin has to offer an opinion, “I thought we were going to return those magical items? We are a fair trade group\!” 

I look at him and wonder how his kind even exists, and shoot. 

Was it the distraction or the natural toughness of the creature, but it’s unaffected. 

“That hurt,” it howls. 

“It can speak?” I say to no one in particular. 

The creature shouts, “I am just trying to get a tasty meal\!” 

Vukradin shouts, “Perhaps we can pay you?” 

“It would take a lot\!” 

“We have very little.” 

The creature snarls, “Maybe this will help motivate you.” It directs its anger at me and fires a volley of tail spikes that hit me. 

Then its voice echoes over the land, “Perhaps this will motivate you to find more money?” 

As I examine my wounds, I hear Vukradin shout a command. The spell doesn’t work. 

And I hear the monster laugh. And then it stops laughing, “I see a human. I will happily take him and leave you alive.” 

A fair trade, I would have thought back in a different life. 

Soma, who cares about everyone of us, shouts, “What?”

“I prefer the succulent taste of human meat to the flesh of other humanoids. Let me have him, and I will leave you and this woman alone.’ 

I wonder what Soma will do, and she casts a spell, conjuring a familiar that she orders to fly into the mouth of the Manticore. The creature snaps its jaws shut. 

The goal was to provide it with a tasty morsel. But all it does is enrage it further. 

“That was not satisfying\! Where’s the meat\!\!\! The blood? The tasty crunch\!” 

Soma is charging. I know that look—the look of a mother who won’t let someone touch her clan. 

Seeing everyone advance, I advance. 

Brewbarry has arrived close enough to throw his hand axes. 

The monster looks at the barbarian and shouts, “Maybe you are tastier” after one of the axes hits the wings of the manticore. And it flies and rends Brewbarry with its claws. Brewbarry simultaneously strikes it with his halberd as it flies in. 

Both antagonists are injured, but it is the manticore that flies to the second floor howling in pain. 

“Please do something,” comes a frantic voice from the first floor of the windmill. 

Soma tries to reassure the woman, “Stay calm\!” 

“Do something,” the woman shrieks. 

Soma stares with that look of confusion, “You could run out while it’s distracted?” 

“It could attack me\!” 

I observe Vukradin wondering what to do. I know that look, the look of a gambler. “Should I try again?” 

Soma is not a gambler. She shouts, “He’s unlikely to avoid falling to your spell twice\! I believe in you.” 

And of course, the Manticore is unaffected. And of course Vukradin is annoyed, “Well, I didn’t study maths or chance\! I studied the arts\! I trusted you, Soma\!” 

The tortle looks hurt, “How can I make it up to you?” she says in her matronly voice. 

“I don’t know if I can ever trust you\!” says the aasimar. 

I stare at Soma, who looks visibly hurt.  

I place another crossbow into my handheld crossbow and shoot, and miss. 

Thankfully, Brewbarry is still alive. He climbs to the second floor where the Manticore is hiding, and hits it twice. The creature howls in pain. And being ignorant, attacks Brewbarry, whose rage protects him from the worst of the Manticore’s claws. 

I notice how the creature seems to be flying away, and I wonder where and there in the distance, I can see Corbin. The beast has decided to eat Corbin.

Vukradin and Soma strike her with their spells. And now the killing blow is all mine, and my hand-held crossbow bolt misses again. 

I stare in disbelief at my crossbow, frustrated. 

“YES\!\!\!” screams Brewbarry. He has killed the Manticore. 

### Vukradin

I cut off the creature’s head and then march to the windmill, the bloody head in tow. 

“Ma’am, you can come out now\!” 

Soma tries her soothing tone, “It’s safe now.” It's the tone of a mother to a small child. 

The woman who greets me at the windmill door is clearly past her prime, though her age is difficult to pinpoint. Her form is that of a commoner, neither remarkably tall nor short, with a lean and perhaps slightly stooped posture, as if weighed down by endless burdens or years spent hunched over work. Her hands, though calloused and bearing the faint, persistent scent of herbs and perhaps antiseptic, seem capable of both healing and, you sense, great precision. Her face, weathered by the winds of Umbrage Hill, is often set in a grim, unyielding line, almost as hard as the stone of her windmill. But it's her eyes that truly stand out: a piercing, perhaps cold, gaze that seems to miss nothing, burning with an inner intensity that hints at her fanatical convictions and ruthless determination. Her hair, likely a practical shade of grey or brown, is pulled back simply, betraying no vanity, only purpose. She wears plain, functional clothing, perhaps stained with remnants of her work, emphasizing her pragmatic nature. 

I straighten up, “Are you Adabra?”

Soma says soothingly, “It’s safe\!” 

And, of course, Valphine tries to be helpful, “I could teach you about Lathander\!” 

“Is it dead?” 

Brewbarry, ever helpful, waves the dead tail. 

I am confused that she didn’t guess we had won when she heard the big thump of a body hitting the ground. She explained that she wasn’t certain if it was one of us the creature had picked up and dropped, or the beast itself. And she was very determined not to tempt fate. 

Soma tries to find out something about how long she has been here under the siege of the manticore, and we discover it’s only been a short time. 

I try to get her to come with us, but she refuses. And just then she rushes back into the building and comes out with a vial and announces, “This is my special potion of healing with extra scent and taste that makes it go down sweeter\!” 

Soma, who lived near a city and saw more than her share of rich people use scents when they bathe, mutters, “That sounds like a bath water potion.” 

That doesn’t help us get her to come to town. She’s very determined to stay here. Insisting that she must stay here to craft her potions. 

There is a deeper agenda at play here—an agenda I don’t quite understand. 

### Soma

I am trying to make up lost time as a druid, and this woman has something about her. She looks at me. 

“You are a tortle?” she asks. And I nod. And then she asks me something very odd, “In the great schism, are you on the naturalist or interventionist side?” 

I don’t know what she is saying, but I sense that in my heart I would be with those who want to preserve, not intervene, and say, “Naturalist.” 

Her aura and sense of being change. There is a sudden shift in her body. 

“Very good.” And then she starts to speak with a zeal about events that I don’t quite understand involving a group called the Emerald Enclave \- “The naturalists, like us, think that the meta-verse is part of the natural order. We should accept the divine interventions as part of the natural order.” 

I look at her, and smile, she just wants to keep things the way they should be, “We should accept this as part of the natural order.” 

“Wonderful,” she sighs. “Now, as part of my role in the natural order, I must stay here and continue to craft potions.” 

Vukradin has other plans and tries to convince her to come with us, explaining that it would be safer for the villagers if they didn’t have to hike out in the open with a white dragon flying about. She smiles and says, “The natural order requires that they come here.” 

Then she stops and looks at me, “You are the ones Townmaster Harbin was looking for? I recall he sent a note to his Lordship asking for help. His Lordship promised that help. Are you it?” 

When we tell her yes, she sighs. “In that case I will stay here, safely protected by you.” I'm not sure if she's mocking us or being earnest. 

Vukradin could convince her through his music, “Can you try?” 

He plays a tune, and it is a good tune. Brewbarry appears delighted. 

“He really loves your music?” I tell Vukradin. 

The Aasimar sighs, “I would survey my customers and ask them to give me a score out of ten. I would only accept money from those who gave it a 10/10 rating. Brewbarry was, in fact, the only customer that ever paid me.”
