I stare at him, aghast. He is a child. A naive babe that needs protecting.  

But Adara seems delighted and exclaims, “How wonderful\! This is truly blessed music\! Aasamirs are truly touched by the Celestial planes.”

And yet it doesn’t change her determination to stay. I wonder if I had had that determination, I would still be back home with my family. So I prepare to leave the windmill. 

“Wait,” she shouts. 

And comes back with a note. 

Vukradin takes it. When she permits him to read it, he reads it out loud: “Thank you, Townmaster Harbin, but I will not be leaving my home. Thank you for your help. Please reward these heroes.” 

And then he says, “Wait, here’s a long-winded description of how to take some medicine. Are you healing him?”

Adabra looks at Vukradin, “Yes.” 

With the note in hand, I shrug and begin the long trek back, when of all people Brewbarry asks if we can spend the night here. 

Adabra squeals in delight, “Yes\! I will make a fantastic meal\! But I need help.” 

### Valphine

Corbin arrives at the windmill. He looks even worse than he did before. And now he smells. 

Vukradin again begins the interrogations asking if he robbed Adabra. Even when Adabra insists no one has ever robbed her, Vukradin persists. 

The inquisition of the Aasimar is exquisite. 

Corbin breaks down, “I didn’t want any of this. I woke up with nothing but the clothes on my back after my family was killed. I came to town, and nobody wanted another broken man. So I went into the forest, and then the crew told me to join. And I joined.” 

So he’s another lost soul. Perhaps Lathander can help. But Vukradin has already tasked him with helping Adabra. 

As the food gets prepared, Adabra stands up, “Well let me show you around. Outside here is an old dwarven house.” 

And of course, Vukradin has to start asking if she stole the house. “We’ve encountered a lot of people taking things, thinking they are entitled.” 

Adabra looks at him, hurt. She explains that the house was destroyed before she came here, that she has a deed to the land, and that she has tended to the dwarf cairns for the dead. 

“I am quite human, not a grave robber. That’s why the manticore wanted me\!” 

Soma, who although younger in years, is wiser, looks at the old woman’s casual specism and mutters, “He thought you were just meat. That’s why he wanted you.” 

But then we learn from Adabra, that Manticore’s actually do have a preference for human meat. 

Imagine that. 

“And you were not adequately trained by your druidic masters. Well then let me help you Soma, the Manticore has a peculiar taste for human flesh over all other humanoids.” 

Soma, whose story of her training is still a mystery to me, looks deflated and grouses, “Whatever.” 

The room is silent while Adabra makes a meal of hearty, fresh-baked bread, a vegetable and herb stew made with local fungi, foraged vegetables, berries, and wild greens.

Overbrighters make the best meals. It’s all because of Lathander’s glory\! The sun-god fuels the ground and the food, and it is \-just- tastier. 

### Soma

Soma was annoyed with Adabra. Her druidic master, Meril, had tried his best in his one year near her home. And it was his prompting that led her to follow Vukradin. Yes, there were gaps, but she didn’t have the time to train because she had so little time left. And to be reminded.

After dinner,I sit and listen to Corbin’s tale of woe as he recounts it to me: “I wasn't born into this life. I was a farmer from a small, forgettable village called Greenmeadow, nestled in the plains east of the High Forest. My life was simple and good; I worked the land my father had worked, was married to a woman named Elara, and had a young daughter, Lily, who loved the wildflowers that grew at the edge of our fields.

Then, the world shattered. The Ordning, which structured the giants' world, broke, and chaos swept across the North. The Giants became emboldened, and lawless destruction ensued. One smoke-filled afternoon, the Uthgardt barbarians of the Black Lion tribe descended on Greenmeadow. They weren't raiding for supplies; they were a storm of pure destruction, a wildfire in human form, proving their strength in a world gone mad.

I fought. I was no warrior, armed only with a wood-axe and a farmer's grit, but I fought for my home and my family. It was not enough. I watched my fields burn, my home collapse into embers, and my family… I watched them fall. I only survived because I was knocked unconscious by a charging barbarian's shield and left for dead in a ditch, buried under the body of my neighbor.

I awoke to silence and ash. With nothing left but the clothes on my back and a soul scoured clean of hope, I began to walk. I drifted south for months, a ghost haunting the roads, taking what I could to survive—a half-eaten apple from a cart, a discarded blanket, a few coins from a sleeping traveler's purse. Each petty crime chipped away at the man I had been, but it was a necessary act to simply keep living.” 

This man's journey through life was changed by visitors. He saw death and horrors. I met Meril. By the grace of the gods… 

I think. And then I sleep. 

## 04-01 Taraskah 1495 

### Soma

And am woken up by Adabra. 

It’s morning. And there is bread on the table. I get up and eat. 

“I’ve got work to do, and you have to go get your reward\!” 

Seeing how she took care of us, I say, “You were the real reward.” 

But Vukradin, who is desperate for money, mutters, “I don’t think we will.” 

She stares at him, flabbergasted, “Well if he doesn’t, come get me and I will give him a piece of my mind\!” 

He looks at her, and I stare at them both as the incomprehension grows, and so I explain, “The bard will only take money from so few sources and he’s desperate.” 

“Why?” Adabra asks us both.

“Because everyone’s pressuring me to kill monsters, take their money. I am not going to do that. That’s stolen property. Rescuing you is organic, conflict-free, fair-trade gold. If you don’t come to town, I am not getting paid.” 

I notice how he feigns a tear. The boy can act. 

“I am never going to get that studio.” 

And then I see the exact change on Adabra when I told her I was a naturalist. She exclaims, “That’s such a wonderful change from all the slaughtering of the interventionist faction of the Emerald Enclave. I’m going to come and support you. Why didn’t you say that was why you wanted me? I did not know you were one of us.”

She takes a deep breath, “This barbaric slaughtering of monsters to seize their treasures is an act of barbarism and vandalism\! It’s a CRIME\!”

I look at Brewbarry, who seems hurt, “I am a barbarian.” 

An opportunity to take her down a peg, “We don’t use the B word in front of Brewbarry.” 

And of course, it doesn’t work. 

“He is not a barbarian. That’s a word for those who destroy the natural world. He is a nomad.” 

Brewbarry seems uncomfortable and tries to insist that he is one. 

“No, you are a nomad. I will not permit such language in this house.” 

Her voice then becomes shrill, as if a deep passion stirs, “The word barbarian implies that there are people who are civilized and those who are uncivilized and that the uncivilized are outside the natural order of things. There is no such thing. The interventionists want to draw lines, and when you draw lines, those that fall out become prey and can be destroyed. You, Brewbarry, are part of the natural world. You are not opposed to it.” 

I notice that Vukradin has the look of a child who heard he was going to get his favorite food, but was unsure, and in that tone he asks, “I heard you were going to come with us?” 

“Well, yes. You are fellow naturalists\!”

# Chapter 05 Vukradin, Rank Cheval 

## 04-01 Taraskh 1495

### Soma

The sun shines, the walk is long and Adabra feels the need to talk. 

“Harbin, bless his heart, wants this area cleared of monsters. And what is a monster to him?”

I want to answer, but whereas Merill would let me think, Adabra has an answer to his question. 

“Anything that disrupts his idea of peace. The manticore, the orcs driven from their homes, they are merely acting as nature intends.” 

She looks at me, as if she wants me to understand something, “It is the meddling that truly upset the balance.” 

I nod. Her wisdom is undeniable. “Let nature take its course. Wolves and deer are going to eat each other. It’s okay.” 

Adabra smiles, “This is exactly what I say, Soma. Some believe we must fight every evil that comes from the outer plane. But where do you draw the line? Do we draw the line at a spirit from the ethereal plane? A fiend from the abyss? Or is it a god’s design? To fight against these is to deny the very nature of existence itself. And when you start denying the right of one thing to exist, you start calling people barbarians.” 

At that, poor Brewbarry sighs, “I was a barbarian\!” 

But Adabra assures him he was never a barbarian; he was a nomad. 

I am worried that this will continue for hours, so thankfully, Vukradin decides to play some music, and this time the music is good.  

### Vukradin

Valphine wanted to play her musical instrument along with me. That may not work for me. Although this time, it added a particular color and texture that elevated my composition to art. Perhaps, we can find a way to collaborate as long as she recognizes her role in our duo. 

And at last we are at the doorway of the Townmaster’s home. And once again, he pleads that a dragon ignore him, and I am about to explain once again I am not a dragon but am interrupted by Adabra.

“Harbin, get out here and pay this young man who has rescued me the money that is owed him.” 

As the Townmaster peeks out from the door, I cough and explain that the mission was more involved than he intimated in his note, and that he could pay us more. 

The Townmaster, reflecting the sordid morality of the area, asks why I didn’t pay myself in Manticore treasure as per the lawful agreement with Lord Neverember. 

I am about to express my outrage, but Adabra is furious \- “Harbin, we have talked about this before. This young man, Vukradin, is no common sellsword, the kind of whom you and Lord Neverember insist on recruiting. He is an idealist, respectful of life, and willing to sacrifice money for his principles. He wants honest wages, fair trade for work done, and conflict-free gold.”

This is turning out better than I could have hoped. I love this woman. To help her cause, I say, “Well, said.” 

She’s on a roll. “You need more than mercenaries. You need champions who care for the greater whole, whose principles, though perhaps untested, are fundamentally sound. This isn’t just an expense, it’s an investment in the moral fabric of Phandalin’s defense\!”

She takes a deep breath and continues, “Those who protect us must do so with a deeper conviction than the possibility of tax-free plunder.” And then with a flourish, “Give this man more coin\! And not just this man, but the tortle Soma who shares so many of my concerns about our world, and the nomad who has been so unjustly treated.” 

I notice how she just skips over Valphine, as if she doesn’t exist. Or is it that something about Valphine annoys her? Is it because she is a Drow? 

### Valphine

Lathander’s light will guide me even if this woman chooses to ignore me. If I were a cleric of Lolth, or if I were in my noble house, she would be dead. But I have moved past that world.  

And now the Townmaster and her talk, and they point at Corbin who is standing next to me. 

Finally, the Townmaster explains that in addition to monsters, the town has been under siege by bandits, and he is short of coins. 

Adabra may ignore me, but her look terrifies the townmaster, who suddenly remembers he can help us and offers free room and board in the Stonehill Inn.  

And so we find ourselves once again in the Stonehill Inn. 

Vukradin, whose presence fills a room, approaches the tavern keeper and offers to play some music. 

As Vukradin prepares to play he shouts, “Toblen, what do your friends call you?”

Tolbien laughs, “Spiderman.”

I look at the man, wondering if he is one of us. I do so like spiders. But no. He explains that as a child, he fell into a spider’s nest where spiders were hatching and was covered in baby spiders. He wasn’t afraid, and the sight of him walking calmly covered in Spiders earned him the nickname. 

In a different time and place, my sisters would recruit him. Or kill him. Or possibly delightfully torture him. 

Vukradin sits down to play, and I ask if I could join him. He assents while reminding me that my role is to support him and his music. 

I nod. 

Vukradin’s music is a discordant mess. The brilliance is there, but it’s too complex for this audience. As I listen to it, I realize that the musical elements I've been working on to fuse Lathanderial Choral music and Prayers to Lolth, which I've called *Choralum Lux Maleficarum,* will be perfect. 

The rich, layered choral harmonies drenched in bright, resonant tones that evoke the warmth and hope of Lathander’s light, interwoven with sinuous melodic lines and subtle dissonances that hint at the enigmatic and sometimes unsettling nature of Lolth’s influence, balance out the complexity of Vukradin’s music. 

Vukradin is at first outraged, and then he sees how the crowd is enjoying the music. And he smiles. 

And I take a chance and sing using my contralto voice, weaving intricate, almost hypnotic lines that feel like a spell or invocation into this music. 

Vukradin raises an eyebrow and builds on my vocals. 

The crowd is silent and watches us perform. 

When we are done, there is applause. 

Vukradin looks at me and says, “Perhaps we should play together.” 

### Soma

As I sit and watch the child Vukradin and Valphine, the oddest of pairings, play music, I think about the forest and my children. 

They are traveling the wide world, and I pray to the gods that they are doing well and have avoided the horrors that have felled the north. 

And as I sit, I hear yet another rumor about the strange goings on in the Neverwinter Wood. 

The Neverwinter Wood reminds me of home, and I am tempted just to go and look at it, or at least convince my group to come with me, but just then, Vukradin overhears another story.  

Later, I would learn his name, Daran Edermath, but he’s known as Silverleaf. He is a tall, lean half-elf with a weathered but noble appearance that speaks of years spent both in the wilds and in battle. His once-dark hair is now streaked generously with silver, falling in a slightly tousled mane that frames a face marked by fine lines and a well-trimmed salt-and-pepper beard. His sharp, emerald-green eyes retain a spark of keen intelligence and quiet wisdom, reflecting a lifetime of hard-earned experience. He wears simple, practical clothing—earth-toned tunics and sturdy leather boots—well-suited for tending what I learn later is his orchard and wandering the countryside. 

Silverleaf tells Vukradin, “You’re an adventurer. I used to be one. Let me share with you a story \- West of Phandalin, on the coast, is an old stone lighthouse. Ships are drawn to this gleaming tower like moths to a flame, and are doomed to crash upon its rocks. Their wrecks must be filled with treasure\!”

Poor Silverleaf, his pitch was wonderful, but he didn’t realize that Vukradin sees Treasure differently, “No\! No\! No\! No\! That’s not treasure.” The boy flops his hands down, “How many times do I have to explain this. You don’t go and rob from the dead and call it treasure\!” 

Silverleaf is in shock and apologizes for offending. Vukradin is on a roll, and I feel for the old elf, but at the same time, lessons need to be learned. 

### Vukradin

This is why adventuring is wrong. When is it a monster? And when is it a poor farmer that you plundered? It’s plunder, and there is no blurry line that makes it right under some circumstances. 

But before I can give my speech, I notice someone new that I had missed earlier. He’s in his early thirties, with a steady and capable presence. He’s carrying himself with some confidence that makes him look larger. He’s got dark hair, he’s clean-shaven, and he has a scar above his right eyebrow. 

He’s not a farmer or likes to spend a fortune on and wear chain mail armor.  

I scrutinize him, and I notice an emblem of a gauntlet grasping a sword by the blade. I try to remember where I saw it before, and I recall something. Yes, I remember. It must be the emblem of a legendary maestro who wields their instrument with such finesse that they grasp the ‘blade’—the sharp edge of sound—directly, mastering even the most dangerous notes\!

A fellow musician, or at least someone who appreciates my music. 

And then I remember something about a group of fanatics, but the details escape me. 

He introduces himself as Ser Kaelen Thorn. Ser wants to talk in private, I insist we do it in public. He shrugs and sits down, and orders drinks from Spiderman. 

“I have heard stories about you around Phandalin and your goals.” 

I smile, clearly a musician, “You’ve heard about my studio that I am trying to build?” 

“No.” 

Well this is awkward. 

“I have heard about your unique perspective on treasure. It’s refreshing in a world that only measures worth in plunder.” 

Valphine seems annoyed or mischievous and blurts, “Or dead drow.” 

Ser notices her for the first time and does a double-take. I am sure this is the first cleric of Lathander he has ever met who is a drow. 

“She’s a good Drow. A cleric of Lathander.”

And then Valphine creeps him out: “I find the sun deliciously painful.” 

For a moment I am worried that he might get up and leave, but Valphine may be the missing link in my music, and I am not going to discard her yet. 

Spiderman brings us drinks, and he takes a sip, stretches back and says, “It’s rare to find one who grapples so earnestly with questions of right and wrong. Where sentients just take the armor off the bodies of the dead without a second thought. We steal their armor in a final act of treachery on the living.” He pauses, “But I sense a deeper conviction in you.” 

“Pleasure and Pain,” whispers Valphine 

Ser Kaelen looks at her as if he wants to uncover the mystery of her existence.  

“Your name is?”

“Valphine.” 

“And you are not a cleric of Lolth or any other underdark deities of horror or hell?”

Valphine looks bored and says, “No. They are very dull. Single-minded in their approach to things.”

Ser Kaelen nods, “I could not agree with you more, they only see the path of death and destruction.” He then turns to me, “I knew you were the right person to talk to.” 

But I notice that Valphine is startled by his explanation. She’s about to explain what she means by boring, but decides to keep quiet. 

I can feel it, he’s going to fund the studio. 

“I serve an order that strives for a better way. Who are we? We are fighters, magicians, storytellers, clerics, all dedicated to one cause, making the north better.”

Maybe if I tell him what I want, “It would be better if I had a music studio?” 

“I am offering something else. What? Imagine what your voice and story would accomplish with the backing of our order. Yes, you can motivate hundreds, but with our backing, you would be known to tens of thousands.” 

### Valphine 

I know this kind. And he quickly explains that his order was instrumental in the War of the Dragon. He brags that one of their order, Milo Goodbarrel, was the leader of the strike force that made it to the inner sanctum and stopped the ritual. 

And then he explains that they are about helping the underdog. And then he says what I know is music to Vukradin’s ear, “Saving the world and not treating it as something to be plundered and taken. We believe that art embodies our mission, and we're confident that through you and your music and story, that message can reach a wide audience. An artist who could make a fortune but turned away from it to do good? You would be a legend\!” 

Vukradin is rightfully dubious, concerned about the sources of funding. And he is assured that it is all conflict-free gold through donations.  

Once the funding sources are clarified, Ser Kaelen explains that Vukradin would at first be an associate member. 

And turning to me, he says, “You too could join.” 

I smile. I don’t think we would work well together. 

Vukradin suggests that Soma might join, but Ser Kaelen’s face turns dark, “She’s a naturalist, and I don’t think that our points of view would align.”  

I wonder about that. 

Vukradin is then told he will receive a pin, and I know the Aasimar will try to sell it, but it’s worth nothing. He's then instructed to continue being true to his mission and opposing the senseless killing and plundering. 

### Brewbarry

Order of Gauntlet. I know them. They fought against my tribe. They killed many. They were proud, dangerous, and ferocious warriors. 

“Order is bullies. They bully barbarians.” 

“We fought a war. A terrible war. It fell upon our order to defend our people from the attacks of your people. It was our kind or your kind. We did not take joy in the slaughter. As I am sure some of your people did not take joy in slaughtering the innocent.” 

“You stole.”  

I want to hit him. 

“A drink? The war is over. And it was brutal. And people died. And it was over nonsense.” 

“Drink good.” 

“Spiderman brings four.”  

### Soma

Vukradin is waiting for a tiny pebble to push him over the edge, and Ser Kaelen provides him with the stone. “Being a member of the order of the gauntlet will get your music out to more people and your message to more people. The combination of your personal story and your celestial origins will be tremendous.”  

Like so many shell-sprouts, time has a way of teaching patience, whether they like it or not. Sit down, sip this tea, and listen, I would tell him. I would explain to him that there’s more to life than rushing headlong into the tide.

But he has already said yes. 

Ser Kaelen responds, “Know this, you are a brother. And when we reach out for help, you must come to us as a brother. And as your brothers, we will come to your help\!” 

## 05-01 Taraksh 1495

### Soma

The shell-sprout is happy. He is part of a family. A family he doesn’t know that wants things he can’t imagine. But now he wants to go on an adventure. 

“We need to destroy the evil tower\!” 

Vukradin is acting like loose-pebble, always rushing into things. 

“The lighthouse is meant to protect the boats, not destroy them.” 

Vukradin shouts, acting like so many mudclingers, “It’s destroying them\!” 

I try to explain to the shell-sprout, “A lighthouse is placed where there is danger to protect ships.” 

But he does not listen. 

And marches out from the Stonehill Inn where we were eating, and marches towards the Townmaster’s place of work. 

The Townmaster, who has not made it to his place of work, sees our Vukradin rushing like a loose pebble down a hill and so stops. 

At first, the Townmaster is confused and then mutters, “It’s a bit of a distance. It’s on the coast. I am very familiar with the tower. I don’t know about the rumors of it being evil. That’s so much blah, blah, blah and rumors.”  

Vukradin holds on to his solution like a tortling clinging to mud to avoid falling, “So how do I destroy it?” 

The townmaster shouts, “Lord Nevermember would be appalled\!” 

Vukradin clings to the mud in his fingers and continues, “Are you saying that Lord Nevermember would permit a cursed lighthouse to remain?” 

“No\! He would want his heroes to remove the curse\!” 

Vukradin stops. I can see him let the mud fall out, “Remove the curse? That’s less work than destroying a lighthouse. How do we remove a curse?” 

“I am not an adventurer, you are.” 

“Ser Kaelen might be able to help. Where is he?” 

The Townmaster tellsChC us that he’s at Barthen’s Provisions, getting ready to leave town. 

Ser Kaelen is delighted to see us. He hears our story and says, “I am delighted to see you take this kind of initiative, Vukradin. But we don’t have very much intelligence about the curse. There are three possible explanations. The first requires a cleric. The second is that it’s some monster that is haunting the place. And the third, the most common, is that it’s just untrue rumors. From what you have said, I think it’s the second.”

# Chapter 06 Conflict-free gold, a curious side quest, and a delightful ambush. 

## 05-01-Taraskh 

### Vukradin

And so we leave for the Tower of Storms. As we round a bend, we spot a small, overturned trade cart, partially obscured by thick undergrowth. Huddled nervously behind it are two figures – a middle-aged human merchant, Elara, and her groom, Jarek. They look visibly shaken and disheveled, their pack horses nowhere in sight.

I approach, and they stare at me with wide eyes, terrified. I take a moment to reflect on our group. Approaching these poor innocents are an Aasimar, a Uthgardt Barbarian, a Drow, and a large Tortle, while the only human looks like a bandit and is wearing armor that he stole from a dead body. 

Sensing an opportunity to make some conflict-free coin, I immediately step forward, reassuringly. 

The woman, seeing that I am obviously a being of principles and not another brigand, cries out, “Orcs attacked us.” 

Soma, whose patronizing motherly tone and lack of refinement are obvious, offers in her guttural voice, “We aren’t orcs.” 

I want to scream, “Well, obviously\!” 

The woman looks at carefully, and asks, ‘Well who are you?”  

And again before I can masterfully handle the situation, Valphine shouts, “Lathandar\!” 

The woman looks confused and then mutters, “Oh ,Priestess\! The faith must be strong in you\!” 

Valpine smiles and adopts that look that so many misunderstood of bliss, “He’s painful\!” 

The old woman looks confused and mutters, “I have never heard that teaching…” 

Calmed down, she says, “My name is Elara, and this is Jarek, my groom and we were heading towards Phandalin…” 

Soma offers to mend the broken cart, and Elara accepts the offer. 

Elara, seeing all of the free help we are giving, asks if we could rescue one of her horses that had run down into a field. Brewbarry, ever the eager companion, rushes off to retrieve it. He's a brute, but a loyal one, especially when there’s a task involving strength or, in this case, a horse.

As Brewbarry runs off, Jarek finally speaks, “I told you we should travel with some protection.” 

Curious about the attack, I ask her to tell me what happened. And as she describes the battle, her eyes dart around, as if she is trying to remember something. She shakes her head and sighs. As she finishes her tale, she says, “They moved with unnerving discipline not like the usual pack I have seen and had odd markings... like a swirl, or an eye?” She shakes her head as if it clear it and continues, “No, it's gone now..."

As for Jarek he also describes the eerie coordination of the attackers, and finishes with this odd note, "I think... I heard something... a sort of hum, not really a sound, just... in my head, before they struck. Then it was gone.”

Valphine says it’s mindflayers, but I dismiss her because she always says it's mindflayers. 

Upon Brewbarry's return with the horse, Elara is relieved. She thanks me for our timely assistance and offers a reward. I hold out my outstretched hand, but she reaches out to Valphine and says, “For the Morninglord and whomever you feel is worthy.” 

I point out to Valphine, “This\! This is Fair Trade and Conflict Free gold." 

The rest of the group wants to press on, but I insist that we return Elara and Jarke to Phandalin. Although there is grumbling, we do just that. 

Upon arrival, we see Ser Kaelen Thorne, who is still in Phandalin and I explain everything to him. He seems pleased that I am not just focused on the big picture, but also doing good deeds, and how that aligns with the broader values of the Order of the Gauntlent. He ends with, “Bringing you into the fold was the right thing to do."

Compliments are always good. 

As I am asked to commission music, and want to know the style of the group, I ask, “Can you share with me a cheer of the Gauntlet?”

He stammers and apologizes, saying that my talents would improve anything the Order had done. 

This piques my curiosity further. And I insist, so he shouts, embarrassed, “ Steal and shield, Heart and band. We stand as one. A steadfast band.” 

“I am more of a magic user. You have magic users?” 

“Yes, we do. This chant is rather embarrassing, that’s why we need your genius\!” 

I smile—finally, someone who appreciates my talent and vision. 

And so I head out from Phandalin and reflect on what has happened. 

Ensuring Elara and Jarek were safely back in town and getting paid for it is the kind of coin I sought – earned through genuine assistance, not through "barbaric slaughtering". It shows me that I can make the money to build my studio and stay true to my principles. 

Like a well-structured song, helping Elara and Jarek helped resolve the discordant tone of this horrible world into a harmony. 

I say to no one in particular, “Even in a world of monsters and mayhem, opportunities exist for a principled artist to earn a livelihood without compromising their ideals.” 

As we pass Barthen’s Provisions on the road to the Triboar Trail, Adabra approaches us. She smiles at me and pulls Soma aside. 

I approach her, but she seems put off this time. I shrug, but overhear her tell Soma \- “You know the old grove past Whisper Woods? Once vibrant, a true blessing of Chauntea. Now... it withers unnaturally. Trees twist in impossible shapes, colors bleeding wrong, and the creatures... they’re not right. Too many eyes, jerky movements, lost and broken.” 

Adabra mutters something about interventionists and the Emerald Enclave. Soma listens carefully and explains that she agrees to help figure out what is going on. 

I hope she asked for money. 

##  08-01 Taraskh 

###  Valphine 

The sun, ever-present and strangely alluring in its intensity, beat down as we resumed our trek towards the Tower of Storms. It was a journey of a few days, each one a test of my patience for surface world banalities.

Elara saw my conversion to Lathander as proof of the ability to transform one into a force for good. She didn’t see as so few do that I saw Lathander as a greater power of pain. 

I may want to create my cult of Lathander focused on this aspect of his power. 

We travel for a few days on the Triboar Trail, which is curiously bereft of travellers or corpses, finally reaching the high road. 

There, we spent the night at Wayside Inn. The current owner of the Wayside Inn is Martisha Vinetalker, a striking half-elf whose pleasing features contrast with her stern demeanor. She is cold, calculating, and charismatic. The bartender is Backes Dunfield, a human with a scarred face and a crooked smile. The cook is Cooragh Struckt, famous for her incredibly tasty, and alarmingly well-spiced, stews and meat pies.

The cook’s dishes don’t disappoint. 

In the morning, we head out to the coast through a trail that Martisha points out. 

The trail takes snakes through the broken, hilly terrain that forms the coastal regions of the Sword Coast. At times, it takes us through unnatural gullies that split the ground in two. 

Vukradin, ever the pedant, mutters that this would only be possible if a river flowed through here, and that this place is too dry for a river. 

I wonder how these overbrighters survive without the Faerzess protecting them from assaults. Magic transforms the land to help the attackers and defenders. Whatever made these cracks is a force of magic. Not just some natural phenomenon.   
And then I see the greatness of Lathander, by offering so much light and land to the overbrighters, he makes them sloppy and enables war and suffering. 

And I feel a pleasant shiver, and I thank Vukradin because he has allowed me to see more of the divine plan of the fiery god. 

One of these unnatural paths goes through a particular tight juncture. A familiar chill prickles my senses—an uncanny intuition of impending ill. My drow upbringing, steeped in the subtle currents of intrigue, rarely lies. 

Brewbarry confirms my intuition and shows the subtle tracks and the tell-tale glint of concealed armor that betrayed hidden figures.

We decide to climb out of the gully, get to the higher ground, and attack from the rear of our would-be ambushers. 

Our duplicitous ambush brings a rare, almost nostalgic, sense of purpose to the otherwise dull task of overland travel. 

I examine the enemy and think, “Bah, orcs, barely worthy of slaughter.” But then, as I look more carefully, I notice an unusual level of organization for typical surface raiders. They are far more disciplined than the chaotic brutes one usually encounters in this crude overworld. They had planned an ambush, where they would drop a rock blocking our exit and then attack from above, into a tight valley that would expose us to withering fire, from which we could not easily escape. How curious. I also note the presence of an orc shaman or cleric. A touch of divine, however crude, always adds an enjoyable complexity to a confrontation.

I strain to overhear them speak, my knowledge of the Orc tongue allowing me to decipher their guttural chatter: we were to be an "easy kill". Who could have told them this? Perhaps the shaman. And then a slight smile touches my lips. How deliciously mistaken they are.  

The engagement began with a peculiar, gentle form of aggression from Vukradin. His Sleep spell manages to incapacitate one orc and their shaman. Then, Soma, with a sudden, powerful transformation, becomes a brown bear, tearing into two orcs with a brutal elegance that speaks of raw, unadorned power. Brewbarry, embracing his rage, engages head-on, delivering powerful blows and shrugging off incoming damage with a barbarian's resilience. This was the kind of efficient violence I appreciate. Violence, my siblings never understood—raw power like Lathander, who keeps the surface world free of the monsters that thrive in the dark. 

I, too, join the fray. My hand crossbow snaps, sending bolts flying. Then, I call upon the gloriously painful light of Lathander, unleashing Fairy Fire to illuminate our foes, granting us advantage against them. The light burned not only their forms but their illusions of safety. It is a beautiful, burning display, a form of pain I find deeply satisfying, for my devotion to Lathander is less about conventional goodness and more about the raw power and sensation of it. 

And then I think that, “Being good is a form of pain against my very nature. How delightful, that to be good is to cause pain, which is to cause pleasure.” 

The combat continues, a chaotic dance of blades and spells, blood and light. This battle was proving to be more... engaging... than anticipated. Like a complex piece of music, this chaos was demanding, and I found myself quite enthralled by its discordant beauty.

It was in the midst of this enjoyable chaos that the orc shaman revealed a singular power, shape-shifting into a boar. A familiar trick, often employed by the less intelligent shapeshifters of the Underdark, but still a moment of delightful surprise. 

How beautiful this battle had become.  A moment of joy, yet also pain. An ambush, with unexpected tactical depth\! This battle is like finding a rare, exquisitely bitter spice in an otherwise bland dish. It elevates the experience, offering a controlled dose of the delightful pain that truly holds my interest as a connoisseur of such sensation.

# Chapter 07 The Tower of Storms: Echoes, Art, and the Serpent's Coil

### Vukradin's Perspective

The wind whips around us as we approach the Tower of Storms, a grim sentinel on its rocky perch. The air immediately fills with discord: three harpies descend, their songs a cacophony that grates on my ears. Before I can process their screeching, one of them, a male harpy dressed in grey rags, begins to sing, and I see Valphine and Brewbarry succumb, a vacant look in their eyes as they become charmed.

This will not do. I act swiftly, casting Silence, a 20-foot radius sphere of pure, blessed quiet. Immediately, the charming melodies are nullified, and the charm loosens its grip on my allies. The harpy in the grey rags, no longer able to weave its magic, stops its performance, though its meager Intelligence suggests it will try again if given the chance. The battle is on, and at least now, we fight on even terms.

Later, as a female attempts to sing, I find myself charmed. Annoying\! But I have an idea. I use my Bardic Inspiration, turning my failure into a success. It feels like failing upward, a perfectly Vukradin maneuver. I then strike the female Harpy with a spell, breaking its concentration and ending its song. This is how a true artist fights—with wit and timely intervention.

I engage the male harpy with the grey rags directly with my daggers, landing one hit but missing a second. It's a frustrating, slow grind. But then, with a flourish, I deliver the final blow to that harpy using Vicious Mockery, quipping, "He is mocked to death. To death." The silence is now truly complete.

We take a much-needed short rest. Brewbarry retrieves his thrown handaxes, which lay "a few feet away", a testament to his—ahem—enthusiastic aim. I reflect on the harpies' "music" during the battle. "Their music is just… They're not joining the Academy, that's for sure". Conflict-free gold is one thing, but listening to that? Unacceptable.

Our exploration leads us to a 15-foot-high empty room. Through a dirty window, I can see shipwrecks below. These possessions, abandoned to the depths, cry out for their rightful owners. I declare my intent to repatriate these items, or at least deliver them to "errors\! Successors\!". Soma dismisses my principles as belonging to a "colonial paradise" or "mercantile" system. She simply doesn't understand the finer points of moral acquisition.

Deeper within the tower, a battle against Moesko, the Orc Anchorite, begins. After Soma transforms into a brown bear and lands some hits, I seize the opportunity to cast Cloud of Daggers, conjuring whirling blades that trap Moesko within a 5-foot cube, inflicting 9 initial damage. He'll take more damage if he stays there. This combat is certainly more dramatic than the harpies, an actual test of our combined talents, if not our sanity, as Moesko responds with a devastating Lightning Bolt and Thunderwave.

### Soma's Perspective

The harpies are a nuisance, their songs a crude manipulation of emotions. As Vukradin's Silence spell takes effect, I see the charm break on Valphine and Brewbarry. This is effective, but these creatures are not bright, so they'll likely continue trying if we leave the sphere of silence.

The combat is a "long… slow battle". I decide against my usual bear form for this tight space. Instead, I transform into a wolf spider, allowing me to scale the tower walls easily. I crawl towards the female harpy, attacking and dealing much damage. The harpies have surprising resilience, but my venomous fangs find their mark. Meanwhile, Brewbarry swings his handaxes, but he struggles to land a blow, missing multiple times. He's a brute, but perhaps needs some lessons in precision.

Later in the fight, another female harpy in blue rags attacks me, causing some damage. I retaliate, striking it for much more, helping to wear it down. When another harpy female starts singing, I must resist, and I do. "Soma's heard better songs". This constant singing is tiresome.

After the harpies are dealt with and Vukradin prattles about "repatriating" shipwreck salvage, I note his mindset: it's either a "colonial paradise" or "mercantile" system. It's a stark contrast to my own naturalist views.

We move through a room with frescoes depicting stormy seas and a "dark and terrible god", then find a stone altar with lightning bolts carved into it and a metal lightning rod. On a nearby ledge, we discover a harpy nest containing a potion of water breathing. Vukradin questions taking "blood money," but it's simply a resource found.

Upstairs, we find the Orc Anchorite, Moesko, seated in a barnacle-encrusted chair, clad in armor made from giant octopus hide, holding an opalescent conch – the very artifact belonging to Miral the Self.

The battle begins. I open with a minor poison spray attack, then, sensing the need for more power, I transform into a brown bear. In this form, I utilize my multi-attack, delivering significant damage to Moesko. He's tougher than he looks, responding with a potent Lightning Bolt that deals staggering amounts of damage (reduced to by half for most of us, thank Mielikki, as everyone but Brewbarry is struck). Then he casts Thunderwave, dealing more damage and pushes me back.

Brewbarry, finally finding his footing, charges Moesko and hits him for some damage, bringing the anchorite down to death’s door. The tight corridor of the tower makes my bear form cumbersome, so I revert. I deliver the final strike, ending the Orc Anchorite's threat.

### Valphine's Perspective

Upon arriving at the Tower of Storms, the air is thick with the cloying, clashing melodies of three harpies. My instincts, honed in the subtle cruelties of the Underdark, scream danger. Immediately, I am charmed by the male harpie’s song, a disorienting, unpleasant sensation. Thankfully, Vukradin's Silence spell descends, cutting off the offending music and freeing me from its influence.

The combat is a protracted, "long… slow battle". I aim my crossbow at the male, critically wounding it for marginal damage. Later, the creature attacks me, then disengages, but I miss my attack of opportunity. I am more successful against the female harpy, hitting it once and then another time to finally kill it. My crossbow is more reliable than Brewbarry's flailing handaxes, which seem to miss consistently. 

After the harpies are dispatched, and Vukradin ponders the "repatriation" of sunken treasure, I notice the irony. These shipwrecks are a result of the tower's curse. The concept of "colonial paradise," as Soma calls it, resonates with my drow perspective—power dictates ownership. 

While searching through the tower, we find a harpy nest containing a potion of water breathing. Vukradin debates taking "blood money," but to me, it's merely the spoils of the fallen. Why would you leave valuable items behind?

We proceed upstairs and discover the Orc Anchorite, Moesko. He sits in a barnacle-encrusted chair, clad in armor made from giant octopus hide, and in his lap rests an opalescent conch, an artifact I recognize as belonging to the undead creature, Miral the Sea Elf. This is the prize.

The battle is fierce. Soma, in her impressive brown bear form, lands significant blows, and Vukradin cleverly traps Moesko in a Cloud of Daggers. But Moesko retaliates with a Lightning Bolt that scorches most of us, reducing my hit points and leaving me battered. It's a sharp, glorious pain, a reminder of Lathander's raw power.

Brewbarry, to my surprise, manages to charge Moesko and lands a hit for some damage, bringing the anchorite to a single hit point. Finally, Soma, shedding her large bear form to navigate the cramped space, delivers the final, decisive strike, bringing the Orc Anchorite down. The conch is ours. The pain of battle has been invigorating, and the reward, tangible.

# Chapter 08 The Beating Heart of the Storm and Whispers from the Deep

The salty tang of the sea still clung to our gear as we descended deeper into the Tower of Storms, leaving the broken sirens and the eerie calm of the upper levels behind us. Moesko, the dark cleric, lay defeated, but there was still a sense of unease that settled over us.

### Soma

My eyes scanned Moesko’s lifeless form. He had been a formidable foe, but now he was just a collection of secrets waiting to be uncovered. There was a strange hole in his chest, a peculiar detail that reminded me of some macabre tale, perhaps from a fever dream or a whispered legend. My gaze then fell upon an opalescent conch resting nearby, its subtle shimmer hinting at its significance. This, I knew, was what Miral sought.

As Valphine meticulously searched his crude living space, a subtle flicker caught my eye. "I found a talisman\!" I declared, pointing to the concealed compartment she uncovered. Brewbarry, with his unexpected perception, quickly discerned the symbols. "So, like, his octopus armor, he kind of worships a giant octopus, huh?" I mused aloud, connecting the dots between the strange patterns and Moesko's attire. The talisman emanated an unsettling energy, something alien and powerful. This object, much like the conch, felt like it needed to be returned to its rightful, and likely equally mysterious, owner.

The air around us remained heavy, but there was a job to finish. I listened as Valphine recounted the strange, pulsating heart illuminating the beacon. The whole situation was surreal, but my focus had to remain sharp. The curse, we believed, was tied to this tower and its dark inhabitant. Vukradin, in his usual, somewhat exasperating way, kept going on about only taking lawfully earned items. I think all money is blood money until proven otherwise, but I kept that thought to myself.

When it came time to address the water, I knew it was my time to shine, or rather, to swim. "I can actually become, like, an octopus," I offered, then quickly reconsidered. "Let's go with giant toad form, that's probably more appropriate." The transformation was quick, my body shifting, muscles coiling and expanding, skin turning slick and green. My newfound form was robust, boasting a sturdy 39 hit points, making me feel confident as I plunged into the churning depths. The water was murky, with only twenty feet of visibility, but my new toad eyes adapted quickly. My goal was simple: find some dry wood to replace the beacon's foul heart.

As I swam towards the first shipwreck, the Star Crossed Lover, my eyes fell upon something gleaming amidst the debris. It was a \+1 halberd, still clutched in the skeletal grip of what must have been the ship's captain. I swiftly secured it, adding it to our growing collection of recovered items. Just then, a shadow passed over me. A Hunter Shark, drawn by the commotion or perhaps by Brewbarry's lack of subtlety, darted towards us. I met it head-on. My powerful bite landed true, dealing eighteen points of damage, though the creature managed to elude my grappling attempt.

The fight was intense. Another shark joined the fray, then a third. One of them landed a solid hit, and I felt sixteen points of damage rip through my amphibious form, dropping me to twenty-two hit points. Despite the pain, I pressed on, my instincts as a toad and a beast driving me forward. I whiffed an attack, but then with a mighty lunge, I struck true against the second shark, dealing twelve points of damage. It was enough. The beast went limp, its body slowly drifting in the murky water. I even managed to grapple the dead shark for a moment, an odd trophy in this underwater ballet of violence.

After the struggle, I realized the waterlogged timber from the wrecks was unsuitable for immediate use as firewood. "It's all soaked\! Like, we'd have to dry it out before we can light it," I croaked, hauling myself onto shore. I found another locked chest clinging with starfish from the Sea Urchin and, in another wreck, yet a third locked chest. I ferried them all to shore, leaving the lock-picking to those with more dexterous digits. Returning to land, I allowed my toad form to recede, dropping out of my Wild Shape. The experience had been intense, and I healed myself, feeling the weariness of battle.

When Miraal appeared to claim her conch, it was quick, almost too quick. "We didn't die\! Yeah, and check out this cool cloak we found\! You know who owns it?" I asked the giant crab, proud of our finds. He then pointed to the halberd, claiming it as the treasure he was going to get for us. It was a bit rich, but I'm not one to look a gift crab in the mouth. Later, as we shared the cooked shark meat, I reflected on the day. I might not be a purist, but I was definitely a survivor, and I had quite the story (and a shark tooth necklace, soon enough) to show for it.

### Vukradin

The grim truth of Moesko's defeated form settled heavily upon me. I believe, fundamentally, in the sanctity of earned possessions. All this treasure feels like stolen merchandise, and I’m determined to find its rightful owners. I am a musician, after all, not a common thief, and I just wanna make a music studio, and I want to do it without stealing something\! My companions, especially Soma, seem less bothered by such ethical quandaries, but to me, the integrity of our actions is paramount.

When we found the opalescent conch, I immediately recognized it as belonging to Miral the Sea Elf. Our quest had brought us this far, and I intended to see it through with honor. As Valphine probed Moesko's belongings, a concealed compartment yielded a dark, iridescent talisman. It was crudely etched with the stylized, jagged lightning bolt of Talos, the God of Storms. This was significant.

As the others ascended the tower, I noted the octopus armor Moesko wore. My initial thought was that it was splint mail, and therefore useless to us, as no one in our party was proficient in such heavy armor. My mind, however, was already turning to the source of the lighthouse's eerie glow. From below, I had seen the lightning rod, and Soma had connected it to the evil god Talos. Bad things happen in this tower, and the lightning rod is part of the curse. We had to break it.

Reaching the very top, I saw the beacon's pulsating green light spill over the sea. Valphine, with her peculiar fascination, stared directly into it, and for a moment, she was blinded. But not before she revealed the horrifying truth: the light emanated from a human heart, several sizes too large—Moesko’s heart, still beating\! This was the very source of the lighthouse's corrupted power. I knew then, with absolute certainty, that this heart, no matter how bright, was evil. My convictions solidified. I shouted, “We need to destroy the heart, guys. Like, that was part of the deal, that we were gonna save the lighthouse.”

I momentarily wrestled with the problem of replacing the light, but then a forgotten melody, a historical song about a lighthouse and a fire, surfaced in my mind. Lighthouses typically had a fire, not a beating heart. The path was clear.

I wasted no time. With a determined resolve, I descended to the lightning rod and smashed it. Then, I made my way to the top and, with a mighty swing, struck the grotesque heart. It was still beating, a resilient organ of corruption. My first attack missed, but my offhand strike landed. The second swing connected, and the heart, with a final, sickening thrum, was destroyed. The light went out. The air felt lighter, cleansed. "Shall we set a fire?" I asked, feeling the return of a proper order. I then cast a light spell to temporarily illuminate the beacon, as a symbol of our intent, and declared, "I'm more of a musician, not really a swimmer," opting to remain on shore while Soma retrieved wood from the wrecks.

From my vantage point on the shore, the murky water offered little visibility. I heard the commotion as Soma engaged the shark. Trying to assist, I focused my bardic magic. "I can cast Vicious Mockery at a creature if I can hear it," My words, aimed to wound the shark’s pride, dealt one point of damage, a slight but satisfying jab. Later, when the sharks proved more numerous, I decided on a different tactic. "Can I try to sleep both of them?" I asked. With a focused strum of my lute, my magic flowed, and both remaining sharks were asleep\! This was crucial. If they take damage, they will wake up, I explained, ensuring my companions understood the new tactical advantage.

As Soma brought the chests ashore, I immediately questioned Valphine: "Why are we opening other people's chests? Those aren't yours." This constant urge to loot grated on me. We have to return them\! I insisted, looking for any markings to identify the owners. The mermaid statue, the spellbook, the wand of secrets—all were treasures that belonged to others. I'm feeling increasingly isolated in this party, I thought, as the others seemed to embrace the 'finds' more readily.

Miral, the sea elf's ghost, finally manifested as we presented her conch. "Thank you, kind ones. My spirit it can finally rest. Moesko was my undoing. But not entirely of his own will. I felt the shadows that moved within his wines, twisting his devotion to Talos into something colder, more calculating. It is not the Strage of the Stormlord that consumed him, but something foreign." Her words sent a shiver down my spine, her warning echoing in the air: "Beware, surface dweller, the true dwellers. The true storm gathers not in the sky, but in the depths below Leilon." She then vanished. The curse of this tower was ended with Moesko's death, but a new, deeper threat had just been revealed.

The giant crab appeared, offering his gratitude for the sharks we'd dispatched. He then noticed Brewbarry's new halberd. "My, yes, you did in fact find the treasure I was going to get for you," he said. "What the hell is that?" I exclaimed, turning to Brewbarry. "He just said it was a treasure that he was gonna go get for you. Where'd you get it?" I tried to persuade him: "What are you doing? You can't use that." It was frustrating, but Brewbarry, as ever, seemed unmoved. I also noted that the shark meat we had was lawfully earned, which allowed us to enjoy it. The magical cloak Soma tried to foist on me, even though it was fashionable and changed colors, I politely but firmly refused. It was not mine to take, no matter how much it tempted me.

### Valphine

Moesko was dead. A moderately successful priestess of Lolth in my former life, I had a keen eye for power dynamics and intrigue, even if my sisters thought me soft for lacking their glee in mayhem. Here, among these surface dwellers, the concept of "loot splitting" was still a subject of contention. "The way I look at it is the party is going to have a four-way treasure split three ways most of the time," I observed, an internal calculation honed by years of drow politics. Personally, I am not a loot whore or a gold digger; I’m just a simple pleasure kind of gal, so the squabbling over gold was amusing, if a bit tiresome.

My gaze, however, was drawn to the subtle details in Moesko's chamber. Poking around, my enhanced senses quickly located a small, concealed compartment between a loose floorboard. Within it, I found a talisman. As Brewbarry examined it, his surprisingly sharp vision picked out a unique symbol on its reverse: an inverted eye from which delicate, coiling lines, reminiscent of tentacles, unfurled. My own investigation revealed a faint divine resonance and a more dominant, unsettling psionic energy burning from its core—something entirely alien to conventional magic. Instead of backing away, I was intrigued. Life is pain, after all, and this was undoubtedly a sensation to be explored. As I focused, a faint rhythmic thrumming emanated from it, like a distant heartbeat, a whisper of unseen forces that stirred my curiosity.

As we ascended the lighthouse, the beacon's pulsating green light immediately captivated me. My fascination with bright light is an intrinsic part of my new devotion to Lathander. I leaned in, staring directly at the marvelous source of pain. The intensity was overwhelming, and for a moment, I was plunged into a temporary blindness. But before the darkness consumed my vision, I caught a glimpse: the green light was not a spell or a gem, but was emanating from a human heart, several sizes too large. It was Moesko's heart, still beating\! It was a powerful, indeed useful, source of light. When Vukradin called it evil, I countered, "I didn't see anything at all; it just seemed like it was light." How could light be evil? Even if it belonged to a malevolent cleric, it served a purpose. "I don't see why we should destroy it. I mean, it's serving a useful purpose," I argued, choosing practicality over abstract notions of good and evil.

Later, from the safety of the shore, I spotted the sharks attacking Soma, who was in giant toad form. My divine powers, though unorthodox, were still potent. I raised my hand and unleashed Sacred Flame upon one of the sharks, dealing five points of radiant damage as it failed its save. When David's sleep spell sent two sharks into a magical slumber, I seized the tactical advantage. "Can I use Fairy Fire?" I asked, my drow cunning coming to the fore. I cast the spell, coating both sleeping sharks in a shimmering, phosphorescent glow. This meant attackers would have an advantage against them, and since they were already asleep, they could not resist. 

I then made a calculated decision. I unleashed a coordinated attac,k combining with Brewbarry, dealing a total of 22 points of damage to one of the sharks.

Back on shore, with the immediate threats neutralized, I turned my attention to the chests Soma had retrieved. They were locked, but not overly challenging for my nimble fingers. Ignoring David's protests about "other people's chests," I deftly opened them. The first revealed a delicate, nine-inch-tall blue quartz statue of a mermaid. The second held a spellbook, an interesting find, though none of us were wizards. And the third, a Wand of Secrets, with an uncanny ability for secret door detection. These were truly valuable discoveries, no matter their origin.

# Chapter 09 Phandalin: Old Debts and New Suspicions.

### Vukradin 

“I need to go back to Phandalin to take care of some unfinished business.” 

Soma looks at me, annoyed. 

“Well, there is the small matter of the Whispering Wood.” 

I look at her, perplexed. I pull out my notebook and return her gaze, “There is no quest or reference to any Whispering Wood.” 

The tortle has a curious expression on her face and then explains, “Shell-Sprout, the woman Adabra, told me of this wood that needs cleansing.” 

“Well, this is the first time I have heard of it. Where is it?” 

Soma tries to explain where it is, and it’s very much out of the way, and I have more important things to do than deal with a corrupted forest.  

But Soma insists, and explains that according to Adabra,  there is a strange, magical blight spreading through it. According to Soma, Adabra said \- “The trees twist in the natural waves, their leaves too bright or too sickly pale, as if… almost as if the colors are wrong. Something is behind it,  whether it's the interventionists or something else, their constant meddling, their zealous rituals, and forceful cleansing around Phandalin and Leilon.”   

I don’t remember this, but I see the opportunity for pay.   

“Another curse\! We are good at curses\! We are the curse-busters.” And then, trying to be discreet, “How much money was involved in saving the Whispering Woods?” 

Soma shouts at me, “Pebble-counter\! Not everything is about money, it’s about keeping the forests in check\!” 

I am annoyed, “The forest will not build my studio.” And then I can’t even, “And most of the treasure we find, I can’t even use for my studio.” I slam my foot down, “So yes, I want to know how money will this pay.” 

Soma shrugs and mutters, “Pebble Counter.” 

“To Phandalin.” 

I stare at Vukradin and Soma, and they look disappointed. 

Perhaps, I pushed too hard, “Look, let’s go to Phandalin and get some information from the Townmaster.” 

Soma stares at me, and then I think, says, “You dry-shell heart. Adabra saw your need and reached out to Harbin to get your money.” 

Then I pause, and remember that this is Adabra, the midwife.

“Yeah, she and I had a connection. She saw what I was trying to do, and she got me more money. And she doesn’t want to help me now?” 

“Pebble-counter, stop and think.” 

I stare blankly. 

Valphine rolls her eyes, “When you put on the pin of the Order of the Gauntlet, and publicly chose a faction, she stopped talking to you and started only talking to Soma.” 

“I don’t trust them.” 

“And neither does she.”

## 09-01 Taraskh 1495

Soma

We arrive in Phandalin and stand in front of the Town Master’s house. The Shell Sprout is upset. As for me, I am here to guide him wherever he wants to go. And I know that this unrooted sprout will never grow the kind of roots he needs. 

Once in the town square, Adabra approaches me. 

She asks if we have ventured to the Whispering Woods. When I tell her no, she is disappointed. 

“This is important Soma.” 

And then walks away. 

Vukradin asks to talk to her. 

She looks at him, bemused, “Of course. What do you need? A token of good health? Is there some woman in a family way that needs to be taken care of?” 

I think, “Did Adabra crack a bard joke?” 

Vukradin doesn’t notice and asks about the order of the gauntlet. 

Adabra stares at where his pin was. He mutters about it being lost. 

“I don’t know very much about them,” he explains.

“What’s there to know?” 

“They appear very mysterious.” 

I laugh, such a shell sprout. He thin-shell mind can’t understand their motivations.” 

“They are pretty transparent.” 

Adabra looks at him and realizes how thin the shell is and takes pity on this shell sprout. 

“They want to make the world a better place. They seem to think the world is in imbalance and that by making it better, things will get better instead of understanding the world is just fine the way it is and that in their attempts to make it better, they make it worse. They think if you change things for the better, they will get permanently better. The more you push on one axis, the worse it will get on another. They are committed to the foolish path of imbalance.” 

I am now worried, “Are they involved with the Whispering Woods?” 

Adabra looks at me, “No, I do not believe it is them. I believe it is the result of the actions of the interventionists meddling in affairs they shouldn’t be.” She pauses, “The order of the gauntlet is too busy chasing dragons, fighting demons, and trying to clear the land for civilization.” And then she turns dark, “ At least when adventurers slaughter a creature, they take its treasures. They kill a creature and cheer their good deed. There is nothing but the kill, and death and their pursuit of some higher ideal that motivates them.” 

And then she sighs, “They do not understand, like Soma and I do, that the multiverse is one thing. That there isn’t good and there isn’t evil, there’s just one thing.” 

Vukradin looks shocked, “You don’t believe there are any good acts?” 

“No, I believe we can each do good and evil. But to change the nature of the world, to strive to change its very nature, forces the powers of evil and good to respond. And those responses hurt everyone. Instead of accepting things for what they are, they challenge the balance, and the forces of evil will respond.” 

Vukradin is very disconcerted, “Why did you help me?” 

“Because I thought you cared about the music. Because you were devoted to the beauty of being. I thought you saw the world the way Soma and I do. But instead, you pick a side. You are not devoted to Music, but to changing the world.”  

Vukradin is annoyed, “Well maybe we won’t deal with the whispering woods.”

I look at him and think echo-ignorer. 

### Valphine 

After our bizarre exchange with Adabra, we head to the Lionshield Coster, where the proprietor Linene Graywind explains to Vukradin that, unfortunately, due to events that he can’t get into, the Lionshield Coster cannot offer the same rich services it used to provide. 

“Before the events of the War of the Giants, I could get you a scroll in a flash. But now, I have to send out messages and feelers and … well it could take a while and there’s no guarantee of results.” 

The idea that we should spend time and money to return goods that others were incapable of holding onto tires me. 

But Vukradin has opinions. None more ridiculous than his conviction that it was Ser Kaelen Thorne who revealed his position. 

He sat in the middle of the square, screaming about how he intended to visit the Tower of the Storms and destroy it. 

But now we have more important things to do. To find a new keeper of the light at the lighthouse. What a majestic and important role. Surely this will be an easy job to fill. And thanks to Lathander’s power, we destroyed the false light\! I am sure the Townmaster will act immediately with praise and gratitude. 

“You live?” says the frazzled Townmaster when he opens the door. 

“Did you realize that there was an infestation of Talos on the coast and a subversion of the lighthouse?”

Harbin seems relieved, “Oh, excellent.”

Knowing the importance of creating alliances with the powerful, I add, “And put a good word in for us.” 

Vukradin seems agitated and dissatisfied, “Perhaps we could take the note ourselves.” 

The fool, we are lowly agents, and if we were to show up at the ruler’s palace, with our tasks incomplete, we are just as likely to be slaughtered as thanked. 

But Harbin saves me the lecture, “I don’t know whether he would want to see yo. He’s a very busy man. But if you insist. There are problems with this town, and you did sign up to come here. I, personally, would not got back Lord Neverember while the town is still unsafe and your mission incomplete.”

A warning if there ever was one. A warning that even Vukradin figures out. 

“Let’s go talk to Ser Kaelen.”

### Vukradin

When we walk into the Stonehill Tavern, Ser Kaelen is delighted to see us. 

“Why?” I ask. And Brewbarry reminds me that they loved my music. 

“True. But very suspicious.” 

And Soma adds, “Because we defeated evil?” 

Ser Kaelen rises, his armor on his body, his brown eyes and entire face smiling, and the scar on his eyebrow barely visible. 

I don’t trust him.

“It was Talos.”

### Soma 

The shell-sprout is not done talking.

Everyone had said that the order of the Emerald Enclave would not arrive. But the hero of the war, Malfire Morazana, convinced Delaan Winterhound to join the war. An army of Treants showed up and helped secure victory. And so we are friends, even if we do not agree on all things.”

The Emerald Enclave thinks that all things are beautiful. Heroism, for them, is an act of defiance against the natural order. We believe that Heroism is an act of necessity to save the world.”

Adabra has been insisting that something is changing the world, and there’s some kind of blight.” He takes another sip, “To be honest, I paid no attention because no one was hurt. This seemed something that only the tree huggers of the Emerald Enclave would care about. It’s a blight. They will manage it.’ 

I stare at him. He is another shell sprout that is wet from his mother’s nest and doesn’t see. He sees a blight and sees nothing.

Quite honestly, I think she’s gone mad.” He leans forward and whispers, “Some of the Emerald Enclave, after the intervention against Tiamat, have declared that the demons themselves are part of the natural world.”

No, chasing down some trees where, for all I know, there are pixies is not the priority. But if you were to look into it, the townsfolk would be happy. We just don’t have the people.”

Smiles, “Of course, I will see what I can do.”
