She pauses and thinks for a moment, and continues, “Now I understand why, after receiving that missive about the House Margaster and their funding of the Order of the Gauntlet, you did not abandon them. You were more of a friend to the Order of the Gauntlet than a member.”  
Her tone worries me, “Again, am I on trial?” 

She laughs, and then in a reassuring tone, “  I'm asking this question because I've come to make you an offer, a suggestion, a potential way for you to become… what's the word I'm looking for? More famous.” 

I smile. 

She continues, “I am a member of the Lord’s Alliance, and“

I interrupt her, “What is the Lord’s Alliance?”

Her jaw drops at my honest question. 

I ask her, “Is it like the Zhentarim?” 

She looks even more shocked. 

I explain, “ I've heard of the Zhentarim, but I haven't met them yet, either. Are you with them?”

She stares at me, confused, and then smiles, “ I had heard so much about you that your passion for music had made you oblivious to the outside world, and I see now it is true.” 

Brewbarry grunts at Jenna and asks her about her weapons. 

She looks at him and says, with contempt, “Blue beerrree? Is that your name? Did I mispronounce it?” 

She mispronounces my friend's name, and I don’t know why. 

Brewbarry turns to her, and asks, “GEEENA? Is that the correct pronunciation of your name?” 

I interject, “JINA\!” 

And she laughs, “It is Jenna, but for you, Vukradin, it can be anything.” 

I stare at her, confused, “Why would you want your name to be confused?” 

“Because I only care about your success.” 

Now it hits me, “You want to be my agent.” And then I think for a moment, “I do need an agent.” 

She smiles with her whole face and says, “Exactly. What can I offer you? I  can get you plugged in to all of the top places in Waterdeep and Neverwinter.  I can have you performing in front of the nobility. I’m sure I could even get you an audience to play for a set for Lord Nevermember Himself.”

I nod, showing a hint of excitement, but not too much. 

At that point, I hear Valphine’s Lathanderian Choral Death Chant mix. I try hard not to focus on it. And the crowd that demanded her a few minutes ago, now chants for my name. 

I turn to her, “I need to get back on stage. My friend is bombing.” 

She looks at me, “Before you go, there is this small detail about your, what is it, fair-trade gold.” 

I look at her, “I am a real believer in that.”

She looks hurt, “I don’t want you to abandon that philosophy. But a refinement would be necessary.  The treasure is stolen, but it's stolen from the people, not from a person. And let the adventurers be the first to reclaim it. And you might think this is another theft, and it would be, except that by taking the treasure and redistributing it as purchases, the adventurer enables the community to grow through the stimulus of this new gold. In short, by purchasing goods, you are returning the gold to the **people** from whom it was stolen.” 

I shake my head, “Yeah, no.  This is not a line I'm gonna cross. I gotta go perform.” I look at her and tell her what she doesn’t want to hear, “Sorry, not interested in compromising my morals, I'm strong on this one. We need to return these items to their rightful owners.” 

She protests, “I could have done so much for you.” 

I turn on the charm and tell her, “ Why don't you reconsider this, because I think this is a good arrangement for you. I could really entertain your nobles, and they'd really think highly of you as my agent.”

She looks at me, and I can see her consider it for a moment, but then the mask she wears goes back on. But there is a softening in her glare. She admires me. She won’t change her tune, but she does admire me. 

# Chapter 16 Blood Money, Clean Gold, and Fine Wine

The party gathered at the tavern to discuss their recent encounter with Sister Kella, an enemy who had offered to work with them against the Carver. Valphine explained that Kella had provided information on how to find the Carver and offered them the reward she was going to give to Lokudus as a down payment for their cooperation. This revelation sparked immediate outrage from Vukradin, who adamantly refused to work with evil people or accept what he considered stolen goods. Despite Valphine’s attempts to explain the strategic value of having an enemy of their enemy as a temporary ally, Vukradin grew increasingly agitated, declaring he needed air and a cigarette before storming out of the tavern. Jena Roscoe observed his departure and explained to the others that Vukradin was a man of principle who believed possessions belonged to their original owners, not to those who found them.

While Vukradin was outside, two pale-skinned, sunburned villagers named Brin Bundlewine and Giles Slipper-Shine approached Valphine with great excitement. They had heard rumors of a drow who worshiped Lathander and believed in the purifying pain of the sun, and they were eager to establish a chapel dedicated to this interpretation of the sun god’s glory. Valphine agreed that founding a temple was a good idea, and the group decided to convert the dilapidated Tresendar Manor into the Temple of Lathander’s Searing Pain of Justice. Harbin Wester, the townmaster and leader of the Privy Council, conveniently appeared and offered to arrange the paperwork for a modest fee of fifty gold pieces. He framed the transaction as a private arrangement that didn’t need to involve the entire council, describing it as simply how things were done in the Overbright. The deal was struck, and Brin and Giles agreed to renovate the temple for twenty-five gold pieces to cover materials, providing their labor for free.

When Vukradin returned from his walk, Harbin quickly claimed that the temple funds had been a community donation, which pleased Vukradin enough that he didn’t question the arrangement further. Jena Roscoe took the opportunity to explain to the party how investing adventuring money back into the community essentially cleaned it, transforming what might be considered blood money into legitimate community improvement. She suggested that perhaps Vukradin could be made to understand this concept with time, as he was young and had much to learn. Harbin, feeling generous after the successful transaction, even offered to buy a round of beer for everyone at the tavern.

The next morning, Vukradin spoke with Ser Kaelen about tracking down the rightful owners of the treasure they had found. Ser Kaelen explained that he was waiting for information from Neverwinter and should have answers in a few days. He suggested the party could check out Mountain’s Toe or deliver supplies to the Logger’s Camp while they waited. The party decided to take on the supply delivery quest, which Harbin had requested for his brother. At Barthen’s Provisions, they picked up two heavy crates filled with dried meats, cheese, bread, ale, and oil, all loaded onto a cart pulled by an ox named Vincent. When Brewbarry noticed there was no wine among the supplies, Barthen suggested they stop at the Falcon Hunting Lodge along the way, which was known for its fine wine.

##  9-02-Taraksh 1495

After a peaceful two-day journey through Neverwinter Wood, the party arrived at the fortified Falcon Hunting Lodge. The compound was surrounded by a ten-foot-high log palisade and featured a two-story main building, a stone tower, stable house, and guest quarters. They rang the bell at the gate and were greeted by Corwin, who introduced himself as the chef and retainer. After seeing Barthen’s letter of introduction, Corwin welcomed them inside and fetched Falcon the Hunter, the lodge’s proprietor. Falcon was a man with impressive mutton chops who expressed great delight at having guests, especially friends of Barthen. He immediately offered them hospitality, including lodging, meals, and access to his fine wine cellar in exchange for musical entertainment from the party’s bard.

When Soma asked about the unusually large fence surrounding the compound, Falcon explained that orcs had left their mountain homes since a dragon appeared in the area and descended into the valley. He noted that the orcs seemed more organized than usual and appeared to be working with evil half-orcs who inhabited a ruined stone manse about ten miles southwest of the lodge. Falcon also shared his philosophy about adventuring, explaining that there were only young adventurers and retired old adventurers, not old adventurers still actively adventuring. He had chosen to retire to this lodge where he could enjoy hunting, entertaining guests, and living comfortably with his fine wine and meals.

During dinner that evening, Falcon casually revealed that he had built his lodge with his share of treasure from a dragon’s hoard that his adventuring group had killed and split four ways. This revelation immediately enraged Vukradin, who accused Falcon of stealing from the people killed by the dragon and then continuing to take money from guests. Falcon was genuinely confused by the accusation, as he didn’t understand Vukradin’s objection to keeping treasure from defeated monsters. He mentioned hearing rumors of a new movement against adventurers using plunder, which he dismissed as nonsense meant to disrupt the ruling elite and move away from the traditional adventuring lifestyle. Vukradin stormed out again, but was eventually called back inside where Falcon demanded an apology. Vukradin gave what appeared to be a sincere apology, though it was actually quite insincere, and Falcon accepted it graciously.

The party was also joined at dinner by Sridar, another drow who was staying as a guest at the lodge. When Valphine asked if she was a cleric of Lathander, Sridar seemed confused and asked if it was some kind of elaborate ruse, which Valphine denied. Sridar explained that she had become a collector of curious artifacts and items that weren’t quite right, particularly those related to planar events. Her fascination had begun after the blink in the Underdark when demons appeared, and she had become deeply interested in understanding planar transformations and disruptions. She offered to pay good money for any information or artifacts the party might have related to these phenomena.

Valphine shared detailed information about events they had witnessed involving a creature collecting strange items, and Sridar was extremely interested, offering thirty gold pieces for the information. When the party showed her the Talisman of Moesko they had been carrying, Sridar immediately identified it as having a definite planar connection and offered one hundred gold pieces to purchase it. After some discussion, the party agreed to sell the talisman, and Sridar also arranged for Falcon to provide three bottles of wine for Brewbarry as part of the deal. This transaction pleased Vukradin greatly, as it represented what he considered fair trade gold rather than blood money.

The conversation turned to theories about why the planar incursions were happening. Sridar speculated it could be magic users, planar entities, or fools meddling with things they didn’t understand, though she admitted she had originally thought it was a natural phenomenon like the Faerzress in the Underdark. When Brewbarry suggested the events might be intentional rather than coincidental, Sridar found the idea intriguing and worth investigating. Both Sridar and Falcon identified themselves as interventionists who believed in actively stopping planar incursions, in contrast to the naturalists in the Emerald Enclave who believed in non-interference even if it meant letting the world burn. Sridar offered to help the party piece together clues if they found more information about the planar events in the future.

Before the evening ended, Falcon mentioned a potential quest involving the half-orcs at the Woodland Mants, offering a pair of boots of elvenkind as a reward. He emphasized that he had purchased the boots legitimately with proceeds from his establishment, not with stolen gold, clearly trying to avoid another confrontation with Vukradin. However, he suggested the party might need more experience before tackling that particular challenge. As the party settled in for the night, Vukradin privately resolved to search for information about the dragon hoard and find its rightful owners, determined to make Falcon understand what he had done by keeping the treasure instead of returning it to those it had been stolen from.

# Chapter 17 Falcon's Hoard and Hidden Truths 

The party undertook a detailed, covert mission when the bard Vukradin decided to uncover the truth about their host, Falcon the Hunter, concerning his claimed past as a dragonslayer and the source of his lodge's funding. The reconnaissance mission began late at night when Vukradin deliberately undertook the investigation alone, knowing his companions were deep in slumber: **Brewbarry was generating the lodge's most consistent nocturnal sound—a thunderous snoring that rattled the guest house timbers** , **Soma was safely ensconced and silent within her shell** , and **Valphine was merely bemused** (or perhaps pretending to be) in her state of sleep.

Vukradin successfully infiltrated the Main Lodge and ascended to Falcon's private bedroom. To prevent being overheard, he ritualistically cast the spell **Silence** over the area, covering both the room and the adjacent hallway. He gained entry to a locked drawer by prying it open.

Within the room and the unlocked drawer, Vukradin discovered several curious and significant items. These included a pair of wooden elven ears attached to a chain inscribed with "my dearly beloved," and a delicate wooden square carved with a labyrinth maze. As an artist preoccupied with intricate structures, Vukradin recognized the maze immediately: it resembled the famous, maddeningly complex structure described in the libretto of "The Undercity Chorale," a forgotten Waterdeep opera detailing the brutal architecture of the city's deepest subterranean levels. The drawer also contained a small iron box in the shape of a remarkably realistic dragon's head. Upon winding a key and opening the box, he found a **brass ring** inscribed with the Elvish word for "lightning." Vukradin noted that the miniature dragon's head was anatomically correct, appearing as if a dragon's head had been expertly shrunk down in size. He speculated this ring must originate from the hoard of the famous blue dragon **Iymrith**.

The investigation continued the next morning during breakfast, where the Falcon Hunter immediately confronted the party about the disturbed drawer. Falcon, unaware that Vukradin was the intruder, declared that the **Cult of Talos** was behind the attempted theft, accusing them of trying to steal the artifact for an offering to their god. Vukradin, with smooth composure, convincingly professed ignorance about the events and the ring's location, allowing Falcon to believe his cover story.

Cornered by the implication that the cult almost stole his treasure, Falcon was compelled to confess the real, less glamorous truth about his past to Vukradin: he was **not a dragon slayer**. He revealed that he was the only member of his adventuring party to escape Iymrith's wrath, and he only arrived at her hoard after it had been plundered by others. He found residual gold scraps and the ring, which he used as "seed capital" to buy land and build his lodge. He maintained the lie that he was a great slayer because the "fantasy of dining with a dragon slayer" was "good for business" and attracted paying clientele who "want to believe the story." This revelation confirmed Vukradin's conviction that the man was a "fraud and an artist. And a thief."

The outcome was a tactical success for the party. Vukradin secured permission to document the ring, reinforcing his principled stance against taking stolen goods. Valphine was impressed, seeing the lie as "perfectly normal" and a display of genius. Soma agreed that the fantasy made guests feel safe and that non-intervention was necessary in this context. The party gathered crucial intelligence linking the ring to Iymrith's hoard, which also involved lightning and the god Talos, providing context for the recurring threats they face in the region. The party was now rested and ready to proceed with their next objective: delivering the goods.

# Chapter 18 To the Logger’s Camp

### 

## 09-02- Taraskh 1495

### Vukradin 

The Falcon Hunter was a fraud and an artist. And a thief, I must never forget that he is a thief. He has a ring in his possession that belonged to someone. 

Somewhere, someone has lost a magical ring. And I will find the owner. 

And it’s then that I realize we have gone pretty deep into the Neverwinter Wood forest. Brewbarry has been dragging the cart with the supplies for Tribar Wester. At first he complained, but ever since the Falcon Hunter filled it with booze, he has insisted that nobody but him touch the cart. 

The sun is high above, and the air is refreshing and cool. 

When we started our hike into the forest, Valphine let Brewbarry march ahead. But now Valphine is marching right next to him. 

I wonder why.

And we move forward. 

A few hours later, Valphine demands we stop. She points ahead where a poorly concealed Orc is in the bushes ahead. 

“I wonder why he’s there?” 

Soma looks at me and mutters, “You are wet-behind-the-shell Vukradin. The orc is a scout for a raiding party. Don’t make any noise. And don’t try to talk to them.” 

Valphine turns to Brewbarry, “Orcs do make such fine slaves.” 

### Soma 

Leaving my clutch behind, I head out and transform into a bear to get a closer look. Hopefully, the orc won’t think I am a threat. 

But no such luck. He sees me and decides to climb a tree. While climbing the tree, he makes hand motions to the north, east, and west. I notice that beyond the scout is a small clearing. And realize that this was an ambush. 

We could still have the advantage if we approach quietly. 

And then I hear Brewbarry stumble through the woods. 

I want to stuff my head in my shell and mutter, but I can’t. The orcs are here, and now whatever element of surprise we have has been lost. 

But perhaps not, the orc next to Brewbarry shouts, “You are a useless turd of a scout. Of all the scouts, I got one who got distracted by a bear\! I only took you because your mother is my mother’s best friend\! Why if it had been up to me…” 

I climb the tree and swipe at him with my claws, and miss, but his foot is so close to my jaws, and I bite the foot. He howls in pain. 

The scout, despite the bleeding foot, disengages. 

I scream Coward, but it sounds more like “ROWARHHHH\!”  

From 10 feet out, he turns and fires an arrow into my flesh, and I feel the sting of pain.  

### Valphine

I advance. I pull out my crossbow. I fire an arrow. I miss. 

### Brewbarry  

The first orc, who wears a necklace of bones,  moves towards me. I have seen such creatures in the north. They are not harmless, and they are dangerous. The first one throws a javelin at me. It lands in front of my feet, I pick it up and split in two, snarling. 

The second orc, who has a scar on his forehead, shouts,  “You were the dumbest scout then, and you are the dumbest scout now.” 

I am enraged. I remember how in my village, I was exiled because of such accusations.

The first orc attacks me with his scimitar and then slips out of range. 

And then the second orc stops moving. Vukradin has cast some magic on him. The orc's eyes glow. And then he moves to attack the scout.  

The orc with the necklace of bones screams, “You attack my brother’s nephew? Are you mad? Who do you think you are\!” 

I am pleased that this Orc Scout will not die thinking he was banished from his clan. If only my clan showed as much compassion as this Orc.   
From where Soma is, I hear a roar and a crash. The bear has jumped from the branch onto the ground and shoved the scout next to the two orcs. 

###  Valphine

Moonbeam. I abhor that light. It is but a pale imitation of the searing pain of Lathander. In fact, it doesn’t hurt at all. It is not sunlight. Even though Soma says it is. 

I know sunlight. I know the pain. 

And my contempt for her spell knows no bounds, as the orcs are barely hurt.  

But my crossbow finally hurts one of these creatures.  

I smile, as an orc scout looks at me, in horror \- “A Drow who worships Lathander. A bear that casts Moonbeam\!” And then he starts to run. 

I think, “Run, little slave. Run.” 

### Vukradin

I am curious to see what the orc I have not charmed will do. Will he attack one of us? Or will he attack the orc attacking his family member? 

So many possibilities. 

“Once I am done killing this goliath, I will kill you\!” 

Brewbarry scoffs, “Bring it on, shrimp.”  

“Who you calling shrimp?” shouts the orc. 

“You\! Because you smell like one.” 

The orc is confused. He has been insulted in a wide variety of ways, but this really confuses me. 

Brewbarray adds, “I don’t know what it smells like, but I know you smell like one.” 

But then the charmed orc is charmed no more. But I am not done playing with him. I cast phantasmal force, and he sees in his head another copy of the orc with the necklace.  

Wonderful, the orc attacks the image of the orc\! The creature is convinced that his erstwhile ally wants him dead.   

The real orc with the necklace screams, “Foul DROW\!” and attacks Valphine. 

It’s a real shame that folks assume that particular races are particularly evil. It is convenient, but a real shame.  

And then I hear some branches break, and Brewbarry has finally become enraged. 

He has decided to protect Valphine. 

### Brewbarry 

Enraged and enlarged, I swing my halberd in a 20’ arc, and scream, “You will not touch my wine.” 

My swing is true, my roar is good, but I miss. 

Meanwhile, Soma has hit one of the orcs. 

And from the clearing, I can hear the scout stop running, turn, and fire his bow at Valphine. The scout misses. 

### Valphine 

I load my crossbow bolt. I aim. I shoot. I miss. 

It is the unholy light of the moonbeam. 

And the scout flees. 

And I chuckle as the orc with the scar strikes air. Vukradin, the bard, has charmed another with his special kind of music. 

He advances to strike with his daggers and misses. No matter the magic of his music, it hurts the orc with a scar, and he dies. 

And then I am struck by another orc, who sees me as the incarnate will of Lolth, and then flees. I have seen this before, this false bravado. In the Underdark, I would hunt him down and kill him. But in the overbrite, he can see just as well as I can.   

Just then, Soma’s jaws clamp down on the orc with the necklace, and I can tell he will not be long for this world. 

I overhear Brewbarry tell Soma,  “This orc was getting ready to flee. I thought you didn’t attack creatures that flee?” 

The poor creature doesn’t understand hypocrisy, bloodlust, and the thrill of killing and maiming. 

But I do, and I will hunt down this scout. 

I race after him, pursuing the fear and the terror. But this is not the Underdark, where I can see and my quarry cannot. And the scout, escapes. 

When I return, I see Brewbarry and Vukradin have captured the orc with the necklace.  

The orc shouts, “We don’t work for anyone. We are independent. We are an independent orc raiding party.”

Brewbarry growls, “You are now barbecue orc.” 

The orc cowers, and I think that Brewbarry has potential as an interrogator. 

“This wasn’t personal. Ever since we were thrown out of our mountain home by that dragon, it’s been an orc-eat-orc world. We used to live near the Ice Spire, in the Sword Mountains. But with the war of the dragons, and then the war of the giants, a white dragon decided that it wanted our home. We had to flee. We ended up in the valley. Our chief has fallen with some half-orc cultists of Talos and many of our tribe followed him. But I believe orcs should work for orcs, and nobody else.” 

I perk up; perhaps there is a connection here to the other Cultists of Talos. And then my mood darkens, this Orc has opinions about his freedom and whom he must serve, no, that must be fixed right away. 

“You work for us.” 

The creature snivels and asks, “Will I get paid?” 

Brewbarry snarls, “You will get paid with your life.” He then grabs the orc and pulls him toward the cart. The orc’s hands are bound on the cart, and he will now pull it. 

Vukradin asks, “What’s his name?” 

And Brewbarry snarls, “Shrimpy.”  

###  Vukradin 

Just a little bit longer until I arrive at the Logger’s Camp and collect my conflict free reward. 

The trees abruptly end, and  the logging camp spreads along the south shore of the river, where a dozen tents are arranged on a sandy beach. Near a deck, a cabin stands with logs stacked under its awning. Older cabins close by have been torn down to leave only stone chimneys and foundations.

I want to scream. Nobody is here. Worse, a grim silence hangs over the camp.

“If I don’t find Triber, I don’t get my money\! This is awful\!” 

Brewbarry turns to me, “Don’t worry, Vukradin. We will find him.”  

### Valphine 

The orc is tied up. And he will cost us supplies, worry, and care. If this were Menzoberanzaan, I would sacrifice him to Lolth now. But Lathander disapproves of such sacrifice. 

Pity. 

It saves so much time and effort. 

# Chapter 19 The Orc Ambush

**10-02 Taraskh 1495**

As the party traveled through the dense forest, Brewbarry and Valphine spotted an orc scout attempting to conceal himself ahead. Soma quickly realized the scout was a lookout for an ambush further up the path. Valphine transformed into a bear and approached the incompetent scout, who panicked and scrambled up a tree while signaling to his companions to the north. The bear climbed after him and bit into him savagely. At the same time, other orcs emerged from hiding—raiders and brigands who immediately began arguing among themselves about the scout’s incompetence and family connections. One raider threw a javelin at Brewbarry, who caught it mid-air, snapped it in two, and growled menacingly at his attacker.

The battle descended into chaos as Vukradin wove enchantments that turned the orcs against each other. One raider found himself compelled to attack his own scout, screaming insults about the scout’s mother while his companions accused him of treachery. Soma leaped from the cart onto a brigand, shoving him backward before calling down a beam of radiant moonlight that engulfed three of the orcs. The brigand, overwhelmed by the magical assault and the family drama erupting around him, screamed that this was the worst idea he’d ever had and fled into the forest. Another raider charged at Brewbarry with his scimitar, landing blows before retreating, while Valphine fired crossbow bolts that mostly went wide of their marks. Vukradin conjured an illusion that made one raider believe he was surrounded by duplicates of his companion, causing him to waste his efforts fighting phantoms until the illusory assault killed him. The remaining raider, confused and terrified by what he called “drow trickery,” attempted to flee but was put into a magical slumber and captured, while the scout managed to escape into the woods.

The party interrogated their prisoner, whom Brewbarry mockingly named Shrimpy, and bound him to their cart. Under intimidation, the orc revealed he belonged to an independent raiding party displaced from their home in the Ice Spire of the Sword Mountains by a white dragon. Since their exile, the orcs had descended into chaos in the valley below, with their chief going mad and various factions forming—some joining the Cult of Talos after their shaman was killed, others becoming brigands, and Shrimpy’s group trying to remain independent. When he asked if he would be paid for his service, Brewbarry coldly informed him that his life was payment enough. The party continued their journey with Shrimpy pulling the cart, eventually arriving at the Logger’s Camp along the river’s south shore. They found the camp eerily silent and completely deserted despite the early morning hour, with tents on the sandy beach, a cabin with stacked logs, and old stone foundations the only signs of habitation. With no one present to sign their delivery notice, the party realized they would need to investigate what had happened to Tibor Wester and the camp’s inhabitants before they could claim their payment.

# Chapter 20 The Spiral’s Grasp

The party gathered at the Loggers Camp to discuss their next move, with Vukradin learning that he had inadvertently built a reputation as a noble adventurer after saving a town from a dragon and advocating for fair wages. Despite his protests that he simply wanted to open his own studio, the public perception had taken hold. The group recalled information about a missing Emerald Enclave patrol and devised a plan to rescue them, crediting the success to Lyra, a low-ranking member they had previously saved, in order to boost her standing within the faction and gain a valuable ally. After debating what to do with their prisoner Shrimpy, who desperately wanted to be released, they decided to transport him to Phandalin for imprisonment, as Tibor the loggers chief refused to take him to Neverwinter.

Following a long rest, the party consulted Joe’s notebook for directions to the Emerald Enclave meeting point and set off through the wilderness. Brewbarry consumed some fermentable mushrooms along the way, entering an altered state of consciousness. They successfully navigated the terrain and arrived at a riverbank where an unnatural, dense fog covered the eastern shore. Standing rigidly by the water was a Teega the Smith with glassy, unfocused eyes who spoke in an eerie monotone about metal bending, minds being cleansed, and waves seeking uniformity. When questioned about the missing patrol, she cryptically mentioned they were trying to fix a leak with a wooden plug and that the current had found them, reforming their brittle thoughts. She drew a mysterious spiral symbol in the mud before her eyes briefly cleared when Vukradin persuaded her, only to glaze over again as she wandered into a nearby glade.

The party crossed the river and immediately felt a strange tingling in their minds, with sounds echoing oddly and light flickering through the shadows in a way that reminded them of a planar anomaly they had encountered before. In the glade, they discovered a grim-looking man wielding a black coral dagger, accompanied by three figures whose movements were unnaturally precise and robotic. The party recognized these individuals as the missing Emerald Enclave patrol, now clearly under some form of mind control. The man, a Cult Fanatic, coldly informed them that they were interfering with necessary adjustments and that the zealots now served a greater purpose. He spoke of a rising current flowing toward Neverwinter and offered the party a chance to submit, but they refused.

Combat erupted as the Cult Fanatic attempted to control Brewbarry’s mind, compelling him to flee, while his mind-controlled warriors attacked with devastating precision. Soma transformed into a massive bear and charged the cult leader, while Valphine channeled healing energy to keep her companions standing. Vukradin raged and attempted to strike down the fanatic but struggled to land a blow. The battle was fierce, with the warriors dealing heavy damage to the party, but eventually Brewbarry broke free from the mental compulsion and delivered a crushing non-lethal strike that knocked the Cult Fanatic unconscious. The moment their leader fell, the mind-controlled warriors collapsed to the ground, screaming and clutching their heads in agony.

The party quickly secured their new prisoners, tying up the unconscious Cult Fanatic and his warriors, who wore green cloaks with gold badges bearing the same spiral symbol. When they attempted to wake the cult leader, they discovered he could still exert control over his minions even while unconscious, causing them to move robotically toward him. Soma pursued the possessed Teega the Smith who had wandered off, tracking her through the wilderness in bear form before subduing her and bringing her back to the group. The party experimented with separating the prisoners and attempting restorative magic, but nothing seemed to break the mind control as long as the Cult Fanatic lived.

Realizing they needed to transport six prisoners back to Phandalin, the party debated their route and decided to keep the Cult Fanatic sedated for the journey, with Brewbarry tasked with maintaining the sedation. They attempted to interrogate the cult leader when he briefly regained consciousness, but he only muttered vague warnings about tides rising and waves coming, refusing to betray his cause. The party searched the prisoners and found they were affiliated with the Kraken Society, based on the spiral emblems they wore.

On the second day of their journey, a large raiding party of Talosian orcs ambushed them, demanding the Cult Fanatic and identifying him as their enemy. The party, noticing the orcs’ wariness of their strength and the presence of a drow among them, negotiated carefully. The orcs explained that the cult leader must be killed, and after tense discussion, the party agreed to hand him over in exchange for safe passage. The Cult Fanatic, given one final chance to explain himself, spoke only of petty squabbles that meant nothing to what was coming. Valphine executed him swiftly, and the orcs took his head as proof of their victory. An anchorite half-orc, a cleric of Talos, identified himself and declared the deceased cultist as one more obstacle crushed by Talos before warning the party to leave their forest.

With the Cult Fanatic dead, the mind-controlled Emerald Enclave members finally awoke, though their minds were still reeling from the experience. One of them, a member of Lyra’s old crew, expressed relief that she had sent the party to rescue them. The warriors described the horrifying sensation of having their thoughts invaded, feeling orders that weren’t their own dripping like poisoned water into their skulls. They revealed they had been forced to steal an inscription that spoke of a drowned gate beneath Yllyn, somewhere deep in the Underdark. The party realized this was connected to the Kraken Society and represented a significant threat.

As the rescued patrol members recovered, Brewbarry, having drunk all of his ale, wondered where he could get more booze. Realizing they were only five miles from the Falcon’s Lodge, he insisted they return to fetch more alcohol. Despite some reservations about the lodge’s atmosphere, the party decided to make the short detour for rest and wine. The rescued Enclave members would need time to recover fully, and the party would need to decide how to present their success to Lyra and the Emerald Enclave, while also investigating the mysterious drowned gate and the rising threat of the Kraken Society’s influence in the region.

# Chapter 21 When Boars Are More Than Just Boars

The party arrived at the Falcon Hunting Lodge with their collection of prisoners and rescued companions in tow. Among them was a disoriented Teega the Smith, two Emerald Enclave guards who had been freed from captivity, and a criminal named Shrimpy. Falcon greeted them with surprise, particularly pleased to see his friend Vukradin had returned safely. The party presented their prisoners, and Falcon was impressed by their success in the field.

Teega the Smith, still confused and suffering from memory gaps, asked who the party was and why she was there. She explained that the last thing she remembered was working at the Wayside Inn, a tavern with an attached forge located on the corner of the High Road and Tribor Trail. Vukradin attempted to recount the tale of her capture and heroic rescue, though his storytelling was only moderately compelling. The woman revealed she had been experiencing blackouts for some time, and that she had been called by something known as “the Kraken,” which promised peace after the endless wars and chaos that had plagued the Sword Coast.

Through careful observation and examination, the party determined that the woman’s mind had been manipulated through psionic means rather than traditional magic. Her brain had been rewired, leaving gaps in her memory and making her susceptible to the cult’s influence. Brewbarry, drawing on his instincts and experience, determined that despite the psionic nature of the manipulation, this was not the work of Mind Flayers. Valphine attempted to intimidate the woman about her poor life choices in following the Kraken cult, while Vukradin tried a gentler approach, offering her a position as a blacksmith for the Church of Lathander. The woman declined the immediate offer but expressed interest in returning to the Wayside Inn first, saying she might visit the church later.

Falcon then shared troubling news about one of his investments. Mountain Toe’s Goldmine, located fifteen miles northeast of Phandalin, had suffered from poisoned waters that threatened to shut down operations. Falcon revealed he was part of a Neverwinter mining consortium that owned the mine, having received a discounted share in exchange for his consulting work scouting the area. The investment had strained his finances considerably, leaving him without ready cash to offer as a reward. Instead, he proposed giving the party a share of the gold mine itself if they would investigate the poisoning and resolve the situation.

The party also discussed the Woodland Manse quest that Falcon had mentioned previously, where orcs and half-orcs had occupied an old manor. The reward for clearing it would be a pair of magical boots. The Emerald Enclave guards expressed urgency about reporting back to their order regarding the planar disruptions, mind-manipulating societies, and the cult of Talos they had encountered. However, they agreed to remain at Falcon’s Lodge for two nights to rest and recover. Vukradin successfully convinced Falcon to provide free accommodation for everyone, reminding him of their future business partnership. The party debated their priorities, with Falcon preferring they address the gold mine first, but ultimately decided to pursue the Woodland Manse quest to obtain the magical boots.

Early the next morning at five o’clock, the party set out for the Woodland Manse, following a trail through the woods. They noted that the mysterious Drow woman who had been interested in artifacts had departed from the lodge during the night. Falcon provided clear directions, advising them to stick to the trail to avoid getting lost. The journey covered ten miles through the forest, and they successfully navigated the path without incident.

The party arrived at a foggy clearing where a crumbling two-story manor stood, nearly hidden beneath thorny ivy. The structure sat atop a six-foot-high stone foundation, with a balcony overlooking the main entrance. Wild pumpkins grew in patches all around the manor, and several wild boars were feeding among them. The boars snorted with contempt as the party approached, and Soma snorted back with equal disdain. Vukradin carefully observed the scene, noting that the boars seemed evenly distributed around the property.

Soma used her ability to communicate with animals to speak with the boars, hoping to learn more about the manor’s inhabitants. The first boar completely ignored him, but a second boar proved more talkative. The creature complained about “new boars” that had arrived recently and didn’t speak proper boar language or respect the established etiquette of the pumpkin patches. The talking boar explained there were real wild boars and orc wild boars, and while he and another boar to the north hadn’t spoken in years, they at least respected each other’s territories. He squinted suspiciously at a third boar to the south, identifying it as particularly rude and new, having appeared only a few days ago. The party recalled that Anchorites of Talos possessed the ability to shapeshift into animals, raising immediate suspicions.

Valphine briefly objected to attacking without attempting to parley with the manor’s inhabitants, but the party decided to test their theory. Brewbarry summoned a beam of radiant moonlight down upon the suspicious third boar. The creature failed to resist the magical effect and was forced to drop its disguise, revealing itself to be an Anchorite of Talos. The talking boar, witnessing this violent revelation, began to flee while protesting that this was not how proper protocol should be handled and expressing concern about his pumpkin patch.

Combat erupted immediately. Valphine struck first, hurling a bolt of radiant energy that struck the Anchorite with devastating accuracy, tearing through its defenses and marking it for the next attack. Brewbarry entered a rage and charged forward with advantage, but his strikes went wide despite his fury. Soma followed up with a successful attack that wounded the creature further, bringing it close to defeat. Vukradin attempted to silence the Anchorite to prevent it from calling for help or casting spells, but the cultist resisted the magical effect.

The Anchorite stepped out of the moonbeam’s radius and shouted loudly to alert others in the manor. Then it retaliated with terrible force, unleashing a bolt of lightning that struck Valphine, Soma, and Brewbarry in a devastating line of electrical energy. Brewbarry called upon his stone-like endurance to absorb much of the impact, while Valphine managed to partially dodge the worst of the blast. Brewbarry, however, took the full force of the lightning and was left badly wounded. As the session ended, the party found themselves in the midst of a fierce battle, with the sounds of the Anchorite’s shout likely bringing reinforcements from within the crumbling manor.

# Chapter 22 From Retreat to Redemption (and Cheese)

## 

The party found themselves in a desperate situation at the Woodland Manse, battered from the first attack, a shapeshifting cultist of Talos unleashed devastating lightning upon them. Valphine called upon her divine powers to heal her companions, restoring their strength just as another Anchorite, disguised as a wild bull, struck Soma and Vukradin with crackling bolts of electricity. As more cultists emerged from within the house and the surrounding area, the party realized they were dangerously outnumbered.

Faced with overwhelming odds and the prospect of more lightning-wielding enemies, the adventurers made the tactical decision to retreat. Vukradin, ever mindful of his potential share in a gold mine, strongly advocated for withdrawal rather than a glorious but pointless death. Brewbarry, swift in his giant form, carried Vukradin to safety while Soma grabbed Valphine and put her on her back, and the party successfully disengaged from the cultists. As they fled, the talking boars they had befriended earlier expressed disappointment that the strangers hadn’t dealt with the impostors who were violating proper boar culture and etiquette.

As the party reached the clearing where Corbin and Shrimpy were waiting, a little bit down the path to the Woodland Manse, they overheard Shrimpy whining. He was trying to argue that the party must be dead, and that Corbin should let him go. The sound of lightning and burning flesh was undeniable. Brewbarry and Valphine were displeased and showed it in their own special way. The party picked up the Emerald Enclave fighters from the Falcon Hunter and then went south to the edge of the forest just a few miles west of Conyberry. From there, they traveled west along the Triboar Trail toward Phandalin, covering nearly thirty miles before stopping to rest and recover from their harrowing encounter. After a much-needed rest to restore their strength and magical abilities, they continued their journey to the small trading post.

Upon arriving in Phandalin, Vukradin called a council meeting to report their findings. They delivered Shrimpy to Town Master Harbin Wester and informed the council about the Cult of Talos at the Woodland Manse, describing the shapeshifting orcs who wielded powerful lightning magic. When the party inquired about the Cult of the Kraken, most council members were unfamiliar with it, though Ser Kaelen of the Order of the Gauntlet expressed concern about the organization and mentioned suspicions of powerful psionic creatures being involved. Jenna Roscoe of the Lords’ Alliance dismissed the Kraken Society as merely a harmless social club for wealthy elites, though Valphine sensed she knew more than she was revealing.

The meeting took a dramatic turn when Adabra learned of the party’s intervention against the Kraken cult. She became furiously enraged, identifying what they had witnessed as a temporal violation and planar distortion. In her view, the party should never have interfered, as such interventions only triggered cascading catastrophic events across the multiverse. She pointed to the Emerald Enclave members’ involvement in the cult as proof that interventionists were fundamentally wrong, then stormed out of the meeting in righteous fury, leaving the council divided. Brewbarry was confused, but Soma was done with her. And soon the party decided that Adabra’s extreme positions were wrong. And that they realized that this was not the last time they would have to deal with her.

Ser Kaelen provided some welcome news, revealing that research at Candlekeep had identified the original owners of one of the magical items the party had previously found on ships. He emphasized that this effort had cost the Order of the Gauntlet considerable time and money, hoping to strengthen their relationship with Vukradin. Though he promised rewards for returning the items, he made it clear the process wouldn’t be straightforward.

Valphine returned to the partially reconstructed church and delivered a powerful sermon that led the congregation into religious ecstasy. However, the worshippers misinterpreted her message about experiencing the glorious pain of Lathander’s light, believing they must stare directly at the sun until blinded to prove their worthiness. When Valphine realized she could cure the blindness with her divine magic, an unintended new sacrament was born—congregants would intentionally blind themselves and then be healed as proof of their devotion. She also placed the severed head of a Kraken Society cultist on a pike outside the church as a warning. Brin and Giles, the two workers helping reconstruct the church, were ecstatic about these developments. At the same time, the Teega the Smith, and Kraken Society member, observing the proceedings, appeared both disturbed and strangely conflicted by the offer of experiencing pain and redemption.

The party then encountered Don-Jon Raskin, a verbose and boastful man who regaled the tavern with tall tales of his past as a gold prospector, miner, fur trader, privateer, and whaler. He shared a long story about attending a barbarian tribe’s party, proudly believing he had been accepted as a member, though the party quickly realized he had been seen as an idiot. Don-Jon revealed he was the new overseer for the Mountain’s Toe Gold Mine, hired by a consortium in Neverwinter—a consortium that Vukradin noticed included at least one person associated with the Kraken Society. Despite his bravado, Don-Jon admitted he knew nothing about the mine itself but had been required by his employers to hire an escort for the journey.

As the party escorted Don-Jon toward the mine, they discovered six dead orcs scattered across the rocky ground within five miles of their destination. Examination revealed the orcs had been killed by extreme cold rather than violence, clear evidence of the white dragon’s presence in the area. The orcs were not Talosians, which considerably boosted Don-Jon’s confidence. When they finally arrived at the mine entrance, marked by a wooden plank carved with its name, they were confronted by two wererats in hybrid form who claimed ownership of the mine.

Don-Jon’s friendly demeanor helped defuse initial tensions, especially after the wererats reacted with hostility toward Valphine for being a drow. The wererats invited the party to meet their leadership deeper in the mine, guaranteeing their safety. There they met Zeleen Varnaster, leader of the Whiskered Gang, who explained that her group had been displaced from their previous home at the Shrine of Savras by approximately sixteen orcs and several ogres—some from a tribe the party had previously angered.

Zeleen proposed that if the party cleared the orcs from the shrine, the wererats would return there and vacate the mine. However, she refused to help reclaim her own home, claiming she was too valuable to risk and offering only two warriors if pressed. When Valphine attempted to negotiate a cheese-for-labor arrangement, Zeleen found the suggestion stereotypical and offensive, though she eventually admitted interest in cheese from the special cow at Butterskull Ranch. Valphine sensed the wererats were lying about their intentions and would likely try to keep the mine regardless of any deal.

Don-Jon initially insisted the mine could not serve as both a living space and a working mine for safety reasons, but Vukradin’s persuasive arguments convinced him that the wererats could nest in one section while working another. The party struck a deal: the wererats would work the mine and live in part of it in exchange for regular cheese shipments from Butterskull Ranch. This arrangement secured the mine’s operation without requiring a dangerous confrontation with sixteen orcs and several ogres, leaving those enemies undisturbed at the Shrine of Savras for another day. The party had successfully turned a potential disaster into a profitable arrangement, though the long-term consequences of their creative solution remained to be seen.

# Chapter 23 The Ale, the Ex, and Axeholm

The party returned to Phandalin after successfully negotiating a peace agreement at the gold mine. Harbin Wester, the Lord Mayor, greeted them warmly and expressed satisfaction with the recent changes in the community. However, his mood turned serious when Brewbarry inquired about the upcoming ale supply. Harbin warned that the dragon occupying the mountains and the resulting orc incursions were preventing farmers from tending their crops, threatening the town's precious ale production for the season.

Harbin presented the party with several new quests, including investigating Dragon Barrow, securing Axeholm fortress, and exploring the Woodland Manse. These missions, he explained, were funded by Neverwinter's tax system and offered rewards that could help Vukradin establish his music studio. When Vukradin questioned the safety of transporting gold from Neverwinter, Harbin revealed the city's troubled history—decades of catastrophes, corruption, and crime that Lord Neverember was attempting to remedy through progressive reforms. Vukradin realized with some embarrassment that he had been so devoted to his musical studies that he had completely missed these major events unfolding around him.

The party then turned their attention to ensuring a steady cheese supply for the wererats at the gold mine. They sought out Petunia, Big Al's prized cow, and through magical communication learned that she missed the alfalfa fields of her former home at Butterskull Ranch. Big Al mentioned that Qelline Alderleaf, a local farmer, had offered to let Petunia graze on her land for one gold piece per week, though he lacked the funds to pay.

When the party approached Qelline to negotiate, they immediately sensed tension. She recognized that Big Al had sent them instead of coming himself and revealed her deep resentment toward him. During his prosperous days at Butterskull Ranch, Big Al's competitive pricing had severely impacted her farm's income. The one gold piece price, she admitted, was deliberately high—a "hurt price" meant to make Big Al suffer financially. After some discussion, she offered to reduce the fee to five silver pieces per week, but only if Big Al came to apologize to her personally.

Returning to Big Al with this condition, the party pressed him about the nature of his relationship with Qelline. Under their questioning, the large man broke down in tears and confessed the painful truth. He and Qelline had once been engaged to be married, but Big Al had abandoned her the night before their wedding. Though he had always loved her, he hadn't been ready to settle down at the time. The party insisted he tell Qelline the full truth, and Big Al, still emotional, picked up Petunia and headed to her farm to make amends. The party wisely chose not to interfere in their private reconciliation.

Later, Lyra appeared in town, reunited with the two Emerald Enclave members the party had rescued. Despite this success, she was deeply discouraged about her leadership abilities, citing the treant incident and her men's capture as evidence of her failures. Vukradin offered her encouragement, and one of the rescued men revealed that the party had claimed it was Lyra's plan that led to their rescue. Heartened by this support, Lyra agreed to let Vukradin help convince the Emerald Enclave of her competence, though they would need to wait until the next day when the organization was meeting.

Ser Kaelen approached the party with important information about the statue they had recovered from the lighthouse. His contacts had identified it as belonging to Elara Seasong Meliame, a wealthy art collector currently attending an extravagant gala in Neverwinter hosted by her eccentric cousin, Lord Cassian Meliame. However, he warned that agents of House Maragaster—a family notorious for demonic alliances—intended to intercept the statue to embarrass the Meliames. Ser Kaelen requested that the party escort the statue to Neverwinter and present it to Elara personally, making sure to mention the Order of the Gauntlet's assistance in hopes of securing future donations. Vukradin, ever the opportunist, considered thanking multiple organizations to maximize potential favors.

That evening, the party performed at the local tavern. While Valphine struggled with her performance, Vukradin's music energized the crowd, and Brewbarry created an entirely new spectacle with impressive physical displays and dance moves that the audience began imitating. Spider-Man, the tavern owner, rewarded them with free drinks and the crowd showered them with applause and coin. After a night of rest, the party prepared for their next adventure.

The following day, they embarked on a journey to Axeholm, traveling across grassy lowlands that skirted the rocky foothills of the Sword Mountains. Cool winds and rain from the Sword Coast made the trek unpleasant, but they pressed on. Upon arrival, they found the entrance to the ancient dwarven fortress—a dark passageway carved into a gray mountain, flanked by towering bulwarks of seamless stone. A rusted iron portcullis blocked their way, and the arrow slits carved into the walls showed no signs of occupation.

Brewbarry attempted to force the portcullis open with an incredible display of strength, but even his mighty effort couldn't overcome the massive stone block jamming the mechanism. The party realized they would need an alternative approach. Soma summoned a rat familiar to scout through the narrow arrow slits, establishing a telepathic link to explore what lay beyond. As the tiny creature prepared to venture into the darkness of Axeholm, the party stood ready to discover what secrets the abandoned fortress held.

# Chapter 24 Where Reality Unravels: Breaching Axelholm

The party arrived at the ancient dwarven fortress of Axelholm, carved into the base of a mountain miles south of Phandalin. Their quest was to open the long-sealed fortress and make it safe for habitation, as Townmaster Harbin Wester had warned that the people of Phandalin might need to evacuate there if the dragon attacks became imminent. Soma summoned a rat familiar to scout ahead, and the creature discovered a winch mechanism inside the entrance that could lift the portcullis gate. As the rat explored, the party heard unsettling sounds emanating from within: a constant low-frequency ticking like a clock speeding up and slowing down, and the scratching of quills on parchment coming from inside the walls themselves. Working together, they attached a rope to the winch and raised the gate, with Brewbarry then spending considerable effort to smash through an inner portcullis door.

Once inside the main hall, Soma's rat familiar revealed a chamber with a forty-foot-high ceiling supported by thick stone pillars, all covered in a layer of dust. The rat perceived strange spatial distortions where distances seemed curiously out of phase, as if moving twenty feet only covered a foot of actual distance. Ballistas were positioned to defend arrow slits, and the light within the fortress appeared mathematically cold and unnatural, refusing to flicker as normal flames would. When several doors opened, grotesque creatures emerged that had once been the dwarven inhabitants of Axelholm. These out-of-phase beings had parchment-like skin covered in shifting ink, gold coins embedded in their flesh, and mouths sewn shut with golden wire or red tape. Their limbs appeared to multiply and move out of phase with reality, giving the impression of six hands and six legs. Soma used her staff to sense the corruption, discovering a planar anomaly that had warped reality within the fortress and driven its inhabitants mad. The creatures muttered constantly about efficiency, their minds clearly broken by whatever had transformed them.

When Brewbarry finally smashed through the door, combat erupted with the out-of-phase dwarves. Valphine called upon the glory of Lathander, her divine power causing several of the creatures to flee in terror despite them not being truly undead. Soma unleashed beams of radiant moonlight and thunderous waves of force that damaged multiple enemies and sent them crashing against the walls. Vukradin provided magical encouragement to his allies while striking with his rapier, causing one dwarf to blink out of existence as space folded in on itself. Brewbarry transformed into his enraged state, becoming Big Brewbarry, and cleaved through the out-of-phase creatures with devastating strikes from his halberd. As the battle progressed, even more of the warped dwarves materialized from the unnatural light, their forms phasing in and out of reality as they advanced on the party.

The combat grew more desperate as the out-of-phase dwarves revealed their most horrifying ability. When one struck Soma, she became paralyzed and experienced the terrifying sensation of being packaged in a box, sealed, and delivered like an object rather than a living being. The other creatures swarmed her paralyzed form, landing critical blows that nearly killed her. Valphine spoke words of divine healing that restored Soma and broke the paralysis, allowing her to transform into a powerful bear and tear through her attackers. Brewbarry also resisted one of these paralysis attempts, hearing a voice in his head saying "incorrect packaging" as he was momentarily knocked into some kind of cold storage before breaking free. Soma caused the ground itself to shake and tremble, knocking several dwarves prone and making the terrain difficult to traverse. The party fought valiantly, cutting down the out-of-phase creatures one by one, but just as they seemed to gain the upper hand, another dwarf successfully paralyzed Soma in her bear form, leaving her vulnerable as the session ended on a dramatic cliffhanger.

# Chapter 25 From Out-of-Phase Dwarves to Mechanical Mysteries

The battle in the mustering hall of Axeholm raged on as the party fought against the twisted dwarves caught in an interdimensional nightmare. Valphine fired her crossbow at one of the out-of-phase creatures, bringing it to the brink of death. Soma, still in her powerful bear form, found herself paralyzed by a dwarf's unnatural touch, but her constitution proved strong enough to shake off the effect. Together, the party systematically eliminated the remaining dwarves, with Brewbarry delivering crushing blows and Vukradin supporting his allies with inspiring words.

After the combat concluded, Valphine took time to tend to the party's wounds, channeling healing energy to restore their strength. The group then began exploring the strange fortress, noting how the spatial dimensions seemed to shift unnaturally, with objects appearing closer than they should at certain distances. Blinking lights flickered on the upper level, and a pervasive stench of death hung in the air. They discovered a narrow tunnel leading upward, just large enough for a humanoid to squeeze through.

Valphine led the party through the cramped passage to an upper level, where they found a ransacked room filled with broken furniture and debris. A blackened fireplace dominated one wall, its chimney rising to the outside world. Investigating the chimney, they discovered it led to the mountain face where they had originally entered Axeholm, though the view offered nothing of particular interest. The party decided to return downstairs and continue their exploration.

Their search brought them to what had once been a dwarven shrine, its walls carved with images of dwarves performing sacred rites. The eastern section had collapsed, leaving rubble strewn across the floor along with the skeletal remains of several dwarves. Among the debris, they discovered a platinum amulet bearing the symbol of Moradin, the dwarven god. Valphine carefully inspected an unlocked steel coffer, finding it packed with silt that protected a valuable potion of superior healing. The party debated whether these treasures should be surrendered to Townmaster Wester or held by the Privy Council for the benefit of Phandalin.

Continuing their methodical exploration, the party encountered a locked door. Valphine skillfully picked the lock using her thieves' tools, only to find the room completely empty. The discovery puzzled them—why would someone clean out a storage room and then lock it? The mystery lingered as they pressed onward through the abandoned fortress.

The party's exploration led them to a grand pillared hall, where Valphine stealthily peered inside and spotted two more twisted dwarves. The air in the chamber felt wrong, filled with a low, tooth-rattling hum like a massive heart beating deep within the stone. Dust on the floor danced in unnatural geometric patterns. Soma struck first, her bear form surprising one of the dwarves and mauling it to death instantly. The party quickly dispatched the second dwarf, but their victory was short-lived.

From behind a limestone throne flanked by granite statues of dwarf warriors, a horrifying figure emerged—what had once been the Dwarven King, now twisted into a three-headed monstrosity. Another corrupted dwarf appeared alongside him. The air rippled like heat haze, and the creatures screeched in pain before recovering. The King moved with terrifying speed, his claws finding Soma and paralyzing her. His three mouths descended in a flurry of bites, and Soma collapsed unconscious, reverting from her bear form.

Valphine channeled divine energy, turning one of the lesser dwarves who fled up the fireplace in terror. Brewbarry flew into a rage, his enlarged form squeezing through the doorway as he engaged the King. Vukradin attempted to assault the King's mind with an illusion of Moradin himself, but the creature's will proved too strong. The King advanced on Brewbarry, suffering grievous wounds from the barbarian's defensive strikes but pressing forward nonetheless. His attacks found their mark, though Brewbarry's rage allowed him to shrug off much of the damage.

Valphine rushed to Soma's side, channeling healing magic to revive her fallen companion. Vukradin tried his mental assault again, this time successfully conjuring the image of a giant bear in the King's mind. The illusion dealt psychic damage and distracted the twisted monarch. In his confusion, the King turned on Valphine, but fortune smiled upon her—every claw swipe and bite attack missed completely. Soma rejoined the fray, and together the party wore down the three-headed horror until it finally collapsed, defeated.

As the King fell, the party felt a surge of power—they had grown stronger from their harrowing experiences. On the King's body, they found a signet ring bearing the Axeholm crest, depicting a hand clutched in a dwarven gauntlet. Valphine recognized it not only as a valuable artifact but also as a key of some kind.

The party continued exploring, discovering a grand dining room with a massive stone table and iron chandeliers whose candles had long since melted away. An alcove contained a deep pit descending sixty feet—a trash chute where the fortress's inhabitants had once disposed of refuse. Valphine identified its purpose, and the party wisely decided not to investigate its depths.

In the adjacent kitchen, they found typical dwarven implements—metal dishware, utensils, and drinking mugs. Most remarkably, a stone sink still functioned, its faucet spouting hot water. Brewbarry examined the water carefully and determined it came from a natural hot spring, a testament to the dwarves' engineering prowess.

Finally, the party entered the smithy, where rusty anvils stood before blackened hearths. A fluttering noise drew their attention to one of the fireplaces, and Valphine investigated. A strange creature emerged—a tiny, mechanical mosquito-like construct with a steampunk aesthetic, complete with a small glass jar containing blood. Valphine carefully subdued the creature without killing it. Vukradin examined the captured construct, his aesthetic sensibilities offended by its unnatural design. He noted markings indicating it was some kind of sampling device, raising troubling questions about who had created it and for what purpose. With this mysterious discovery in hand, the party prepared to delve deeper into the secrets of Axeholm.

# Chapter 26 Sisters Against the Machine

The party continued their exploration of the ancient dwarven fortress, finishing their survey of the first floor. They discovered a storage room filled with serviceable armor and weaponsmith tools that would prove useful for the people of Phandalin, along with privies. The barracks held dozens of meager cots scattered about, with two cold fireplaces whose rubble-choked chimneys rose one hundred twenty feet through the mountain. An empty armory revealed that the dwarves had taken all their weapons when they departed, leaving behind only stone weapon racks, headless mannequins, and iron hooks on the walls.

Having thoroughly explored the lower level, the party ascended to the upper floor, where the time and spatial distortions seemed more pronounced. As they climbed the stairs, they heard a curious scratching sound echoing from the north hallway, like a hand frantically scratching on paper. Valphine led the group westward into a chamber where they encountered six out-of-phase dwarven figures who screamed incessantly about efficiency and processes. When Vukradin attempted to convince them that the party had come to help improve their efficiency, the dwarves became even more agitated, as if the very concept of increasing efficiency was the source of their torment.

The battle that followed was fierce but brief. Brewbarry charged forward in a rage, his halberd cutting down the spectral dwarves with brutal efficiency. Vukradin wove magic that slowed the remaining enemies, making them sluggish and vulnerable. Valphine called upon radiant guardians that bathed the room in glorious light, destroying two of the dwarves instantly and wounding another. Soma joined the fray in bear form, her claws tearing through the weakened enemies. Within moments, all six dwarves had been dispatched.

As the last dwarf fell, a new threat emerged from deeper within the chamber. The Chief Accountant appeared—a luminous dwarven figure who glitched and flickered like corrupted data, her face a mask of shifting geometric shapes with ink-like shadows leaking from her eyes. Her voice was an unsettling blend of a grandmother's warmth and screeching static as she spoke of ledgers that wouldn't close and regulators dividing by zero. She looked at Valphine and called her "sister of the sun," accusing her of carrying the scent of bleach and betrayal. The party engaged her cautiously, with Vukradin summoning a giant adding machine to attack her while Valphine's radiant guardians continued their work.

The Chief Accountant's retaliation was devastating. She unleashed a terrible wail that echoed through the chamber, and both Valphine and Vukradin collapsed unconscious from the supernatural assault. Brewbarry and Soma weathered the attack, though they were wounded. As Soma moved to stabilize their fallen companions, the Chief Accountant's demeanor suddenly changed. She stared at Valphine's unconscious form with what seemed like panic, frantically attempting to stabilize her with blue-white static energy while crying out about acid damage and depreciation, terrified that "the auditor" would liquidate her for closing Valphine's account. After this outburst, she became incorporeal and fled through a closed door into another room.

After the party had healed their wounds and rested, the Chief Accountant cautiously emerged and began to explain what had happened to the fortress. She revealed that Valphine's sister Aletra, the fourth daughter of the Satora family, had made a deal with the king to improve the mine's efficiency and profit margins. The king had been jealous of the Lionshield Coster's multi-dimensional merchant operations and their incredible revenue. Aletra had promised that installing a special machine would solve everything, but instead the machine had broken and unleashed chaos throughout the keep. The Chief Accountant admitted that when she had complained to Aletra about the books not balancing, Aletra had laughed at her—and then likely killed her. She offered the party a deal: she would give them the override code to shut down the machine if they would let her go and not tell Aletra what had transpired.

The party debated whether to trust the undead accountant, but ultimately decided to follow her directions to the machine. They descended back to the lower level and made their way through a tunnel to reach the machine room. What they found was extraordinary—a massive contraption of brass, orange organ pipes, spinning copper centrifuges, and twisting mechanical arms bolted to the floor. The device vibrated violently, venting jets of purple steam while a magical voice boomed from its brass horn about non-Euclidean geometry and purging protocols. The air was thick with static electricity that made their hair stand on end.

Standing calmly beside this chaotic machine was a drow woman in a high-collared uniform, typing on a glowing keypad with one hand while holding a rapier in the other. Valphine recognized her immediately—not by sight, but by scent. The faint, sickly sweet mixture of lavender perfume and chemical bleach from the Satora family poison labs could only belong to one person: Aletra. Above her, four spectral spiders made of flickering static clung to the ceiling, hissing like white noise. When Aletra turned to face them, Valphine saw the sharp cheekbones and cold violet eyes of the sister who had exposed traitors not for honor, but for profit.

Aletra warned them not to approach, explaining that she was in a delicate equilibrium with the machine and its guardian constructs. She revealed that she needed to extract something important from the device before they could use the override code to shut it down. Through careful observation, Valphine realized what her sister was truly after—drow poison that Aletra had been smuggling through the multiverse using the machine. Aletra spoke to Valphine in Undercommon with her characteristic condescension, telling her to go play in the mud with the other surface dwellers while the adults handled their deadline. She then made her proposal: if the party would kill the spectral spiders that guarded the machine, she would extract her cargo and allow them to disable the device. If they refused, she warned, she might be forced to attempt the extraction anyway—which could cause the entire place to explode. The party stood at a crossroads, weighing their options as they faced Valphine's dangerous and unpredictable sister.

# Chapter 27 When the Machine Screams: A Family Affair

The party found themselves in a tense standoff with Valphine's sister, Aletra, who was working to extract a mysterious package from a broken planar machine. The room was covered in interplanar spider webs, and six Rift Weavers—spider-like creatures bound to the ceiling—stood guard over the malfunctioning device. Aletra explained that the machine had been a gift to her boss and was causing dangerous spatial anomalies throughout the area. She claimed they were in a "spatial equilibrium" and warned that if she couldn't retrieve her package, she had no reason to destroy the machine, leaving everyone to face the consequences of its catastrophic failure.

As the party prepared to engage the Rift Weavers, Valphine attempted to slow the creatures with magic, successfully hampering three of them. Brewbarry and Vukradin moved into position while Soma summoned a sphere of roiling flames that scorched several of the spiders and began burning away the webs. However, Aletra revealed her true intentions when she pointed her wand at Brewbarry, causing him to glow with an ominous red light. The machine immediately detected him as a spatial anomaly, and all the Rift Weavers turned their attention toward him, fixated on eliminating the perceived threat. Aletra had manipulated the situation perfectly, using the party as pawns while she worked on the machine in relative safety.

The battle intensified as the Rift Weavers attacked Brewbarry relentlessly. One of the creatures managed to ensnare him in sticky webs, restraining him while others attempted to bite through his defenses. Valphine cast protective magic on Brewbarry, granting him resilience against the onslaught, while the Rift Weavers used their cosmic abilities to free themselves from the slowing effects. Aletra shouted to Valphine, reminding her of a previous trap they had set together using a stuffed creature as bait, suggesting she simply needed to keep Brewbarry alive long enough for Aletra to complete her work. The drow sister continued manipulating the machine, cursing its dwarven creators for their inefficient design.

Soma's flaming sphere proved crucial in the fight, as the party discovered that the Rift Weavers were deeply disturbed by magical fire. The sphere not only damaged the creatures but also burned through the webs restraining Brewbarry, preventing future attempts to ensnare him. When Valphine struck one of the spiders with radiant energy, it recoiled violently, revealing another vulnerability. Aletra observed this with sardonic amusement, making a cutting remark about their mother saying Valphine wasn't the sharpest tool in the shed, though she did enjoy being the target of pointy tools. The sisters exchanged barbs even as the battle raged around them.

Brewbarry and Vukradin fought with devastating efficiency once the webs were cleared, their weapons cutting through the Rift Weavers with brutal precision. The creatures chittered in frustration as their attempts to restrain the party failed repeatedly, their webs burning away in the magical flames. One by one, the spiders fell, dissolving into crackling sparkles as they were destroyed. The remaining Rift Weavers became confused, torn between attacking Brewbarry and the malfunctioning machine itself, which was beginning to emit warnings of catastrophic failure.

As the last of the Rift Weavers fell, Aletra successfully extracted a box containing vials of interdimensional poison—part of House Sartorra's illegal drug trade. She called out to Valphine, asking if she had the shutdown code and urging her to use it. With dark humor, Aletra remarked that she would hate to have to collect Valphine's body parts and bring them back to their mother, then admitted she unfortunately couldn't leave any evidence behind. She pressed a small device, opening a shimmering portal before her.

In a desperate attempt to stop her sister's escape, Valphine struck Aletra with a blinding curse. Though Aletra had positioned the portal directly in front of herself and managed to step through despite her sudden blindness, the spell caused her to fumble and drop several of the precious vials onto the ground. As she disappeared through the portal, she muttered something about "the boss" not being happy with this development. Aletra's final words acknowledged that Valphine had at least tried to stop her, which was better than simpering and crying like the last time, though she couldn't quite remember if Valphine had been moaning in pain or pleasure during that previous encounter.

With Aletra gone and the machine screaming warnings of imminent catastrophic failure, Valphine rushed to the keypad and entered the shutdown code. The machine immediately ceased its alarming countdown and began to fold in on itself, collapsing and shrinking as it prepared to return to whatever dimension it had come from. The party watched as the device completely disappeared, leaving behind only a small piece of paper—a bill from "Interplanar Trade Consultants Incorporated" detailing payments for services rendered. The remaining Rift Weaver, having nothing left to repair with the planar device gone, simply winked out of existence.

The party stood in the now-quiet room, surrounded by the aftermath of battle and the dropped vials of poison that Aletra had left behind. The spatial anomalies that had plagued the area were finally resolved, though questions remained about the true nature of the machine, Aletra's mysterious boss, and what other schemes the drow sister might be involved in. The bill from the interplanar trade consultants suggested that the machine's presence had been part of a much larger operation, one that extended far beyond the immediate conflict they had just resolved.

# Chapter 28 Drones, Dread, and Dangerous Deliveries

After the interdimensional device collapsed into the void and Aletra escaped, the party searched the room where the machine had been. Nothing remained of the device itself, but they discovered strange strands of interdimensional spider silk left behind by the Riftweavers. Valphine, a former devotee of Lolth, considered collecting the unusual silk for her temple. The party debated the nature of these creatures—whether they were a natural phenomenon, a defense mechanism against planar damage, or summoned beings sent by some unknown deity.

The party opened a door to the west and discovered Aletra's makeshift quarters in what had once been a barracks. A high-quality silk bedroll and a folding desk made of black Zurkhwood cluttered with modern parchment revealed where she had been working. The lingering scent of lavender mixed with perfume identified the space as belonging to House Xorlarrin's poison operations. Soma investigated a ledger on the desk and uncovered Aletra's forgeries—she had crossed out "iron for 500 pounds" and written "Midnight Tears \- crate 4 \-  do not drop," providing clear evidence of her tampering with the books.
